Chapter 10

下一页 >
1.
Where Are the Rabbits? One of the most remarkable features in our domesticated races is that we see in them adaptation, not indeed to the animal’s or plant’s own good, but to man’s use of fancy. . . . The key is man’s power of accumulative selection: nature gives successive variations; man adds them up in certain directions useful to him. In this sense he may be said to make useful breeds. Charles Darwin, On the Origin of Species, chapter 1, “Variation Under Domestication” Despite the enthusiasm for activity that has swept business and financial America, we will stick with our ’til-death-do-us-part policy. It’s the only one with which Charlie and I are comfortable, it produces decent results, and it lets our managers and those of our investees run their businesses free of distractions. Warren Buffett, annual letter to shareholders, 1986
《兔子去哪儿了？》 家养物种最显著的特征之一，是它们展现出的适应性并非为了动植物自身利益，而是服务于人类的实用或审美需求……关键在于人类具有累积选择的力量：大自然提供连续的变异，人类则将这些变异朝着对自己有利的方向积累。从这个意义上说，人类确实培育出了有用的品种。 ——查尔斯·达尔文《物种起源》第一章"家养状态下的变异" 尽管积极进取之风席卷美国商界与金融界，我们仍将坚守"至死不渝"的投资准则。这是查理和我感到自在的唯一方式，它能带来稳健的回报，也让我们的经理人及被投企业管理者能够心无旁骛地经营业务。 ——沃伦·巴菲特1986年致股东信
2.
In October 1988, Forbes published a list of the four hundred wealthiest Americans.1 Sam Walton was the richest with a fortune of $6.7 billion, and Buffett was ranked tenth with $2.2 billion. The list was full of familiar names, including Gates, Helmsley, Hillman, Kluge, Mars, Newhouse, Packard, Perot, Pritzker, and Redstone. But who was Shelby Cullom Davis? Almost no one had heard of him. And how was he ranked as high as 197 while being a new entrant? Davis was tucked between the famous names of Joseph Albertson, the founder of the Albertsons stores, and Fritz Otto Haas, the founder of the global multinational chemical company Rohm and Haas. But what had he founded? Forbes mentioned that he was worth $370 million, was from Tarrytown, New York, and had created his wealth from investment banking. However, Forbes was not entirely correct. Shelby Davis was not an investment banker. Unlike everyone else on the list, he was not an entrepreneur and did not own a business.
1988年10月，《福布斯》公布了全美最富有的四百人榜单。山姆·沃尔顿以67亿美元身家位列榜首，巴菲特则以22亿美元排名第十。名单上尽是耳熟能详的名字：盖茨、赫尔姆斯利、希尔曼、克鲁格、玛氏、纽豪斯、帕卡德、佩罗、普利兹克、雷石东。 但谢尔比·库洛姆·戴维斯是谁？几乎无人知晓这位新晋富豪。这位首次上榜就位列197名的神秘人物，究竟有何来头？他的排名夹在艾伯森超市创始人约瑟夫·艾伯森与跨国化工巨头罗门哈斯创始人弗里茨·奥托·哈斯之间。可此人创立过什么企业？《福布斯》仅提及他身价3.7亿美元，来自纽约塔里敦，财富源于投资银行业务——这个说法并不准确。谢尔比·戴维斯并非投资银行家，也不同于榜单上其他企业家，他既非创业者，也未曾拥有实业。
3.
He was an investor like Buffett. But the similarity appeared to stop there. First, Buffett was a professional investor managing money for others, whereas Davis invested his own money (or his wife’s). Second, Buffett started investing in his early twenties, whereas Davis did not start investing until he was thirty-eight years old. Third, Buffett had studied finance and investing under the great Benjamin Graham; Davis had had no interest in economics or finance during his college days. Instead, he had majored in history and had a special love for the Russian Revolution. Finally, Buffett had spent his entire career investing; Davis had had at least five careers before age forty. He reported for CBS Radio (his first assignment was interviewing Amelia Earhart), was a freelance writer, and was a stock analyst (a “statistician”). He worked at the War Production Board in Washington during the Second World War and was a deputy superintendent in New York State’s insurance department.
他与巴菲特同属投资者之列，但相似之处似乎仅止于此。首先，巴菲特是替他人管理资金的职业投资人，而戴维斯只运作自有资金（或其妻子的资产）。其次，巴菲特二十出头便开启投资生涯，戴维斯却迟至三十八岁才涉足投资。再者，巴菲特曾师从本杰明·格雷厄姆研习金融与投资，戴维斯大学期间却对经济金融毫无兴趣，主修历史专业并痴迷俄国革命研究。最后，巴菲特毕生专注投资事业，戴维斯在四十岁前已至少转换过五份职业：担任过CBS电台记者（首个任务是采访飞行员阿梅莉亚·埃尔哈特）、自由撰稿人、股票分析师（自称"统计员"），二战期间供职于华盛顿战时生产委员会，还担任过纽约州保险厅副督察长。
4.
Even Davis’s investing style was radically different from Buffett’s. Buffett invested across a range of industries, whereas just one sector contributed to Davis’s colossal wealth; Buffett invested in very few businesses in the United States, whereas Davis invested in at least 1,600 businesses worldwide and occasionally traded heavily. But there was one way in which Davis and Buffett were alike. And it made Davis wealthier than most people who have ever lived on this planet. Darwin: The Unappreciated Math Wizard Darwin was a mathematical genius. But he didn’t think so.
戴维斯的投资风格与巴菲特截然不同。巴菲特涉足多个行业投资，而戴维斯的巨额财富仅来自单一领域；巴菲特在美国只投资极少数企业，戴维斯却至少投资过全球1600家企业，且时常进行大额交易。 但戴维斯与巴菲特有一个共同点。正是这个特质，使他比地球上绝大多数人都更富有。 达尔文：被低估的数学奇才 达尔文是个数学天才。但他自己并不这么认为。
5.
On July 29, 1828, the nineteen-year-old Charles Darwin wrote a letter to his close friend and second cousin, William Darwin Fox. He started with a complaint and then rued his lack of mathematical prowess: “What excuse have you to offer for not having answered my letter long before this? I hope it is nothing worse than idleness; or what would be still better, I hope it arises from your being ten fathoms deep in the Mathematics, and if you are God help you, for so am I, only with this difference I stick fast in the mud at the bottom and there I shall remain in status quo.”2
1828年7月29日，十九岁的查尔斯·达尔文给挚友兼二表哥威廉·达尔文·福克斯写了封信。他先埋怨对方迟迟不回信，继而哀叹自己数学不济："你这么久不回信，能找出什么借口？但愿不过是犯懒罢了；要更好些呢，我巴不得你是埋头钻研数学十寻深。若真如此，愿上帝保佑你——我也是这般情形，只不过我陷在泥沼底层动弹不得，怕是要永远困在这境地了。"
6.
Darwin reiterated his weakness in mathematics in his autobiography: “After years I have deeply regretted that I did not proceed far enough at least to understand something of the great leading principles of mathematics; for men thus endowed seem to have an extra sense.” He also admitted that the subject “was repugnant to me.”3 He detested complex mathematical formulations and once wrote to a friend, “I have no faith in anything short of actual measurement and the Rule of Three.” The Rule of Three is a simple mathematical calculation that answers the problem “If ten mangoes cost $8, how many mangoes can one buy for $40?”
达尔文在自传中多次提及自己在数学上的短板："多年后我深感遗憾，当初至少没能深入学习到领会数学重大基本原理的程度；具备这种素养的人仿佛拥有第六感。"他也坦承这门学科"令我反感"。他厌恶复杂的数学公式，曾写信告诉朋友："我只相信实际测量和三率法。"三率法是一种基础算术方法，用于解决诸如"若十个芒果售价八美元，四十美元可买多少个芒果"这类问题。
7.
I regard Darwin as a math genius because of his intuitive grasp of the prodigious power of long-term compounding. Most of his peers didn’t understand it; in fact, neither did many of his successors. In chapter 3 of Origin, “Struggle for Existence,” Darwin’s exquisite grasp of the power of compounding is evident in his famous example of elephants. He wrote, “The elephant is reckoned to be the slowest breeder of all known animals, and I have taken some pains to estimate its probable minimum rate of increase: it will be under the mark to assume that it breeds when thirty years old, and goes on breeding till ninety years old, bringing forth three pair of young in this interval; if this be so, at the end the of fifth century there would be alive fifteen million elephants, descended from the first pair.”
我将达尔文视为数学天才，源于他对长期复利巨大力量的直觉把握。他的大多数同辈未能理解这一点，事实上，许多后继者同样未能参透。在《物种起源》第三章"生存斗争"中，达尔文通过著名的大象案例，精妙地展现了其对复利效应的深刻理解。他写道："大象被认为是已知动物中繁殖最慢的物种，我费尽心思估算其可能的最低增长率：假设它三十岁开始繁殖，持续到九十岁，期间产下三对幼崽；若果真如此，到第五个世纪末，最初那对象的后代将有1500万头存活于世。"
8.
Like no one else before him, Darwin understood that an exponential increase of populations was theoretically possible but practically almost impossible—diseases, predators, lack of food, natural disasters, and many other factors kept populations in check. This realization led him to conclude that only the fittest variants would survive to pass on their traits to their offspring. These fitter variants would then start exponentially increasing, leading to evolution through natural selection. As he famously wrote in chapter 4 of Origin, “This preservation of favorable variations and the rejection of injurious variations, I call Natural Selection.”
达尔文前所未有地认识到，种群数量在理论上虽可能呈指数增长，现实中却几乎无法实现——疾病、天敌、食物短缺、自然灾害等诸多因素制约着种群规模。这一洞见使他得出结论：唯有最适应环境的变种才能存活并将特征遗传给后代。这些更具适应性的变种随后会开始指数级繁衍，从而通过自然选择推动进化。正如他在《物种起源》第四章的经典论述："我将这种有利变异的保存与有害变异的淘汰，称为自然选择。"
9.
As I discussed earlier, Darwin’s theory of natural selection had no place for sudden and dramatic changes. His theory required variations to be small and continuous and natural selection to work over very long periods through accumulated changes. Despite its glaring simplicity and explanatory power—or maybe because of it—his theory remained on the periphery of biological sciences during his lifetime and was not entirely accepted by the scientific community.4
正如前文所述，达尔文的自然选择理论并不认同突变式的剧烈变化。该理论认为变异必须细微且连续，自然选择需通过漫长岁月中的累积变化发挥作用。尽管这一理论具有惊人的简洁性与解释力——或许正因如此——它在达尔文有生之年始终处于生物科学的边缘地带，未能完全获得科学界的认可。
10.
In 1900, after the rediscovery of Gregor Mendel’s work on heredity, Hugo de Vries, a well-respected Dutch botanist and geneticist, proposed a new theory of evolution called mutationism.5 According to this theory, the slight continuous variation proposed by Darwin could not lead to the evolution and creation of species; only significant mutations could. In his Die Mutationstheorie (The Mutation Theory), de Vries claimed that new species arise suddenly owing to discontinuous alteration. He wrote, “The new species thus originates suddenly[;] it is produced by the existing one without visible preparation and without transition.”6
1900年，在孟德尔遗传学研究被重新发现后，荷兰著名植物学家与遗传学家雨果·德弗里斯提出了名为"突变论"的新进化理论。该理论认为，达尔文提出的渐进连续变异无法促成物种进化与形成，唯有显著突变才能实现。德弗里斯在《突变理论》中宣称，新物种会因不连续的突变而突然产生。他写道："新物种由此突然诞生[；]它由现存物种直接产生，既无可见的准备阶段，亦无过渡形态。"
11.
Now that everyone could understand. Intellectually, this was a much simpler assertion to understand than Darwinism because it could be “visualized”—Darwin’s gradualism couldn’t be. The world of investing is eerily similar. Everyone seems to know that the stock price of AMC, a movie theater chain, tripled in May 2021, but how many know that Home Depot’s multiplied 140 times over thirty years from 1990 to 2020?
现在所有人都能理解了。从认知层面看，这比达尔文主义更容易理解，因为它是可以"具象化"的——而达尔文的渐进论则无法做到。投资世界与此惊人地相似。人人都知道连锁影院AMC的股价在2021年5月翻了三倍，但有多少人了解家得宝从1990到2020三十年间股价翻了140倍呢？
12.
According to mutationism, species are created not because of minor variations but because something big and strange happens that transforms the organism. The controversial debate between mutationism and Darwinism remained unresolved until the 1920s. Finally, mathematics rescued biology (who would have thought!). In the 1920s and ’30s, the theoretical geneticists R. A. Fisher, J. B. S. Haldane, Sewall Wright, and a few others explained in complex mathematical language how continuous variation was compatible with Mendel’s laws. Natural selection, acting cumulatively on minor variations, could produce significant evolutionary changes over surprisingly short periods.7 These acknowledged mathematical geniuses restated what Darwin had asserted almost fifty years earlier.
突变论认为，物种的形成并非源于细微变异，而是由于某种重大而奇特的事件彻底改变了生物体。这场突变论与达尔文主义之间的争议持续到1920年代仍悬而未决。最终数学拯救了生物学（谁能料到呢！）。在1920至1930年代，理论遗传学家R·A·费希尔、J·B·S·霍尔丹、休厄尔·赖特等学者用复杂的数学语言阐明：连续变异与孟德尔定律并不矛盾。自然选择通过持续作用于微小变异，竟能在极短时间内引发显著的进化改变。7 这几位公认的数学天才，用公式重新论证了达尔文在五十年前就已提出的观点。
13.
He was saying that if a particular variation—say color vision—could give an individual a slight advantage over its peers, almost the entire population would be able to see in color over many fewer generations than we would imagine. Let us assume that color vision has a “selective advantage” of 1 percent, meaning that individuals with this trait produce 101 viable offspring instead of 100 (maybe color vision allows the individuals to locate higher-quality fruits in the forest). Thus, the selective advantage here is equivalent to compound interest or annualized return. The advantage accumulates and grows exponentially over generations. Thus, in the second generation, the 101 offspring with color vision produce 10,201 offspring who can see color (101 x 101), whereas the 100 “normal” offspring produce 10,000 “normal” offspring (100 x 100). This slight advantage compounded at 1 percent per generation yields dramatic change over time.
他指出，如果某种变异——比如色觉——能让个体获得微弱的生存优势，那么只需比我们想象中少得多的世代数，几乎整个种群就会演化出彩色视觉能力。假设色觉具有1%的"选择优势"，即具备该特征的个体能繁衍101个可存活后代，而非普通个体的100个（或许色觉能帮助它们在森林中定位更优质的果实）。这种选择优势类似于复利或年化收益，会随着世代更迭呈指数级累积增长。 因此在第二代，101个色觉个体将繁衍10,201个色觉后代（101×101），而100个普通个体仅繁衍10,000个普通后代（100×100）。每代仅1%的微小优势经过复利积累，最终将引发巨大的演化变革。
14.
Suppose there are eight individuals with this trait (i.e., color vision) among a thousand individuals. Over how many generations do you think color vision would spread to 90 percent of the population? Only 3,000!8 Thus, if this were an organism with a life span of one month, most of this species would have color vision within 250 years with just a 1 percent selective advantage. In evolutionary terms, this is almost instantaneous transformation. And this is not just theory.
假设一千人中有八人具有这种特质（即色觉）。你认为色觉需要多少代才能扩散至90%的种群？仅需3000代！因此，若该生物寿命为一个月，仅凭1%的选择优势，这一物种中的大多数个体就能在250年内获得色觉。用演化论的术语来说，这几乎是瞬间的转变。而这不仅仅是理论。
15.
Scientists observed the rapid evolution of peppered moths in Manchester in Britain in the nineteenth century.9 Peppered moths were generally white with small black splotches on their wings. They rested on lichen-covered tree trunks during the day, where they were camouflaged against birds, their main predator. The species also had a rare, black-colored mutant. But it did not survive long because it was visible to birds against the background of tree trunks. As a result, most populations of peppered moths were, well, peppered. But as Manchester became industrialized from the middle of the nineteenth century, air pollution blackened tree trunks, thereby reversing the advantage: The black mutant became invisible to birds, and the peppered form stood out. The first black peppered moth was recorded in Manchester in 1848, and by 1895, 98 percent of the population had become black. The cumulative impact of a slight advantage had converted the rare form into the dominant one. Interestingly, as Britain passed strict pollution laws in the middle of the twentieth century, trees began to lose their sooty coating. As a result, the black moth has become rare, and the peppered form is now dominant!
科学家观察到十九世纪英国曼彻斯特地区椒花蛾的快速进化现象。这种蛾子通常通体白色，翅膀上带有黑色斑点。它们白天栖息在长满地衣的树干上，斑驳的体色成为抵御主要天敌鸟类的天然伪装。该物种还存在一种罕见的黑色变异体，但由于在树干背景下容易被鸟类发现，这种突变体难以存活。因此绝大多数椒花蛾都保持着斑点外观。随着十九世纪中叶曼彻斯特工业化进程，空气污染使树干变黑，竟意外扭转了生存优势：黑色突变体在煤灰覆盖的树干上获得隐身效果，而原本具有保护色的斑点形态反而显露无遗。1848年曼彻斯特首次记录到黑色椒花蛾，到1895年该地区98%的种群都已变成黑色。微弱优势的持续累积，最终使罕见变种成为主流。耐人寻味的是，随着二十世纪中期英国通过严格的反污染法案，树干逐渐褪去煤灰外衣，导致黑蛾重新沦为稀有品种，斑点形态再次占据主导地位。
16.
This kind of microevolution (e.g., a change in color), given enough time, can lead to macroevolution (i.e., the creation of a new species). There isn’t a single mathematical formula in Darwin’s Origin. Still, it captures the power and essence of long-term compounding better than the complex formulas of the geneticists. Amazingly, a mathematically challenged naturalist could figure out what had eluded scientists over the millennia by applying a simple yet profound mathematical concept to the natural world: Compounding creates life—all of it. But why is this relevant for us investors? Because compounding also creates wealth. Almost all of it. The Assault on Australia We think we understand compounding, but we don’t. By “we,” I mean the investment community, myself included. Although Nalanda’s entire investing strategy rests on the pillar of slow and steady compounding over decades, even I am amazed at its stunning—even surreal—results when applied over long periods.
这类微观演化（如体色变化）若经历足够时间，便能催生宏观演化（即新物种的形成）。达尔文《物种起源》中虽无一道数学公式，却比遗传学家那些复杂方程式更精妙地捕捉了长期复利的精髓。令人惊叹的是，这位数学能力薄弱的博物学家，竟通过将简单而深邃的数学概念——复利创造生命，世间万物皆源于此——应用于自然界，破解了困扰科学家数千年的谜题。 但这对投资者有何启示？因为复利同样创造财富。世间财富几乎尽出于此。 **澳洲启示录** 我们投资界——包括我自己——总以为已参透复利真谛，实则不然。尽管那澜陀投资数十年来的策略根基正是缓慢而稳健的复利积累，但当我目睹其在超长周期中产生的惊人——近乎魔幻——的效果时，仍会感到震撼。
17.
Before we proceed any further, I want you to appreciate its tremendous power. Then, I will highlight two surprises, one small and one big, that cumulative growth has in store for students of evolution and investing. For this section, I will be an omniscient consultant (are there any other kinds?) in the nineteenth century, and you will be a savvy time traveler from 1925! Who said investment stories couldn’t be exciting? Let’s now go back in time to Winchelsea in Australia in 1859, where I am an adviser to one Mr. Thomas Austin. Mr. Austin has imported twenty-four rabbits from England, and he wants to release them into the wild for sport hunting. He is an intelligent fellow and is wary of the rabbits’ prodigious reproductive ability. As he does not wish the farmland in Winchelsea to be overrun by rabbits, he seeks my counsel.
在我们继续深入之前，我希望你能理解其巨大的力量。接着，我将揭示累积增长给进化论学者和投资者准备的两个意外——一个较小，一个较大。 在本节中，我将化身为19世纪无所不知的顾问（难道还有其他类型吗？），而你则是一位来自1925年的精明时空旅者！谁说投资故事不能激动人心呢？ 现在让我们穿越回1859年澳大利亚的温切尔西，当时我正担任托马斯·奥斯汀先生的顾问。奥斯汀先生从英格兰引进了24只兔子，打算放归野外供狩猎消遣。他是个聪明人，对兔子惊人的繁殖能力心存警惕。由于不希望温切尔西的农田被兔子侵占，他前来征求我的建议。
18.
Just as I am about to advise him to release the rabbits, I see you swooping in from the future to issue a dire warning: “I come from 1925 and see a catastrophe ahead. Don’t release the rabbits.” On further inquiry, you reveal that the whole of Australia is in peril because of these twenty-four creatures. I laugh at your facetious remark, ignore the warning, and ask Mr. Austin to release the rabbits. You promise to visit me every five to ten years to continue to warn me about exterminating the rabbits. You fulfill your promise, and every time you come to see me, I ask the same question. Table 10.1 captures the history of our interactions. Table 10.1The first thirty-five years Years after 1859 No. of rabbits Your advice My response 5 108 Kill them before it’s too late. Where are the rabbits? 10 482 Kill them before it’s too late. Where are the rabbits? 20 9,700 Kill them before it’s too late. Where are the rabbits? 35 900,000 Kill them before it’s too late. Where are the rabbits?
正待建议他放出那些兔子时，却见你从未来疾驰而至，发出严厉警告："我来自1925年，预见一场浩劫。切莫放出这些兔子。"细问之下，你透露全澳大利亚都将因这二十四只生灵陷入危难。我对你的戏言不以为意，未加理会，仍请奥斯汀先生放生兔子。你承诺每五到十年便来见我，持续警告我铲除兔患。你信守诺言，而每次相见，我总抛出同一问句。表10.1记录了我们交锋的历程。 表10.1 最初三十五年 1859年后年份 兔子数量 你的谏言 我的回应 5 108 趁早灭杀，为时未晚 兔子在何处？ 10 482 趁早灭杀，为时未晚 兔子在何处？ 20 9,700 趁早灭杀，为时未晚 兔子在何处？ 35 900,000 趁早灭杀，为时未晚 兔子在何处？
19.
Thirty-five years go by, and I continue to gloat over the fact that you have been proven wrong. There are fewer than a million rabbits in about eight million square kilometers of land area, and they don’t seem to pose any imminent danger. But you warn me that the historical growth rate is about 35 percent a year, and at this pace, Australia will be overtaken by rabbits in the not-too-distant future. As is my custom, I ignore the genie from the future. Table 10.2 tells the story of the next thirty-one years, until 1925. Table 10.2The next thirty-one years Years after 1859 No. of rabbits Your advice My response 45 17.5 million Kill them before it’s too late. I can see some. 55 350 million Is it too late? No, it’s not. 66 10 billion I told you so. @#$%*!
三十五年过去，我仍在沾沾自喜——事实证明你错了。在这片八百万平方公里的土地上，野兔数量不足百万，似乎构不成什么迫在眉睫的威胁。可你警告说，历史增长率是每年35%，照这个速度，澳大利亚被兔子占领不过是迟早的事。依照惯例，我再次无视了来自未来的预言。表10.2呈现了此后三十一年直至1925年的发展轨迹。 表10.2 三十一年间的发展 1859年后的年数 野兔数量 你的建议 我的回应 45 1750万 趁早消灭它们 还能应付 55 3.5亿 现在太迟了吗？ 不迟 66 100亿 早警告过你 @#$%*！
20.
This is a true story. Unfortunately, the twenty-four rabbits released by Mr. Austin in Australia in 1859 did produce ten billion rabbits by 1925 and wreaked havoc on the flora and fauna of the continent.10 Despite more than one hundred fifty years of government efforts ranging from building fences, trapping, shooting, and conducting biological warfare (by releasing flies with the deadly myxoma virus), Australia has been unable to eliminate this pest. I said that there were two surprises in this story. The small surprise, at least for me, is that twenty-four rabbits became ten billion. At some intuitive level, we investors understand that compounding can lead to astronomical numbers given enough time. But even then, I doubt many of us would have been able to envision a number of ten billion rabbits in the mid-1920s when there had been fewer than a million in 1895.
这是一个真实的故事。不幸的是，奥斯汀先生1859年在澳大利亚放生的24只野兔，确实在1925年繁衍到了百亿规模，给这片大陆的动植物生态带来了毁灭性灾难。尽管政府持续150多年采取围栏阻隔、陷阱捕捉、射杀乃至生物战（投放携带致命粘液瘤病毒的蚊蝇）等手段，至今仍未能根除这种祸患。 这个故事有两点令人震惊。较小的意外（至少对我而言）在于24只野兔竟能增殖到百亿规模。作为投资者，我们在直觉层面都明白：只要时间足够，复利效应能产生天文数字。但即便如此，恐怕也没多少人能预见到——1895年尚不足百万的兔群，竟能在二十世纪二十年代中期突破百亿大关。
21.
The bigger surprise—which is also counterintuitive—is the opposite observation: Nothing happened for a very long time! After twenty years, not many rabbits would have been visible in Australia, and even after forty-five years, there were fewer than two rabbits per square kilometer. So Australians ignored the rabbit problem for many decades because rabbits did not become a problem.
更令人惊讶且反直觉的是与之相反的现象：在很长一段时间里，一切风平浪静！二十年过去后，澳大利亚境内几乎看不到多少兔子；即便四十五年后，每平方公里仍不足两只。正因兔子未成灾患，澳大利亚人对兔患问题置之不理长达数十年。
22.
This property of compounding—that its impact seemingly remains hidden for a long time—wreaks havoc on the performance of investors because most sell too soon. An investor can hold a great business for five years, multiply their money three times, and then sell off for two potential reasons. First, they think that they have made enough and that there are better fish in the sea. Second, they get tired of the slow progress. (After all, the share price of GameStop can jump seventeen-fold in a month!) Little do they realize that if the share price had continued to climb at the same rate, in twenty-five years, they would have made 243 times their money! I know that that is a big “if,” but it isn’t an insurmountable hurdle for a quality business, as we will soon see. Also, even if the incremental return from the fifth to the twenty-fifth year in this example falls by more than five percentage points, the investor would still make 100 times their money on the original investment! As I said, the bigger mystery of compounding is not that it leads to large numbers but that it doesn’t do so for a long time.
复利这一特性——其影响在很长时间内似乎隐而不显——严重扰乱了投资者的操作表现，因为大多数人过早抛售。一位投资者可能持有一家优秀企业五年，资金翻了三倍，随后却因两种潜在原因选择卖出。首先，他们觉得已经赚够了，认为还有更好的投资机会。其次，他们对缓慢的进展感到厌倦。（毕竟游戏驿站的股价能在一个月内暴涨十七倍！）他们很少意识到，如果股价继续保持这样的增速，二十五年后收益将达原始本金的243倍！我知道这个"如果"的假设很大，但对于优质企业而言这并非不可逾越的障碍，后文将予以说明。即便本例中第五年至第二十五年的年化收益率下降超过五个百分点，投资者仍能获得原始本金100倍的回报！正如我所言，复利更大的奥秘不在于它最终产生巨额回报，而在于这个爆发过程需要漫长的等待。
23.
The holding period of most funds is barely a few months, let alone years. If you explain this behavior to an intelligent noninvestor type (I have done so), they will find it rather odd. They say something like this: “You are telling me that it is tough to find great companies to invest in; you are also telling me that these companies can grow their profits reasonably predictably over long periods. So why would you sell such a company in a hurry after you have become fortunate enough to own it?” I haven’t had a good answer to this question except, “My community is not willing to wait for the rabbits.”
多数基金的持有期仅有短短数月，更遑论数年。若向一位聪慧的非投资人士解释这种行为（我确实这样做过），他们会觉得相当怪异。他们会这样说："你的意思是找到值得投资的优秀公司很难；你还说这些公司能在长期内以相对可预测的方式增长利润。那么为什么你幸运地持有这样一家公司后，却要急匆匆地卖掉它？"对此我始终没有令人信服的回答，除了这句："我们这行人等不及兔子撞树。"
24.
I have seen too many people make a profit of 50 to 100 percent on an investment in a great company and then press the exit button. We investors take pride in being math savvy. Mention the word “compounding” to us, and you will get knowing smiles. Unfortunately, most of those knowing smiles do not seem to know that what they know about compounding—that it can lead to big numbers over time—hides two great unknowns. The first is that compounding does not lead to significant numbers for a very long time. The second is that investing would be easy if companies could compound predictably. But, alas, they don’t. The real world is quite messy, and the path to long-term success is treacherous, unpredictable, and full of disappointments. What is needed to become a successful investor is not intellect, a commodity, but patience, which is not. Many More Reasons We Don’t Sell
我见过太多人在一家优秀公司的投资上获利50%到100%后就匆忙按下退出键。我们投资者向来以精通数学自居。只要提到"复利"这个词，就会看到大家心领神会的笑容。可惜的是，大多数会心微笑者似乎并不明白，他们自以为理解的复利原理——即随时间推移能产生巨大收益——背后隐藏着两大认知盲区。 首要盲区在于：复利效应需要极长时间才能显现惊人威力。其次，倘若企业真能稳定实现复利增长，投资将变得轻而易举。但现实总不尽如人意，真实世界错综复杂，通往长期成功的道路布满陷阱、充满变数，更伴随着无数挫折。 成为成功投资者所需的不是智力（这种泛滥的禀赋），而是稀缺的耐心。 （我们坚持持有的）更多理由
25.
Are we not convinced yet? With the power of compounding in evolutionary theory as the background, let me present some more reasons we are permanent owners in great businesses. “I will never sell” would be an understandable sentiment from a passionate entrepreneur, but it is somewhat unusual—some may even say wrongheaded—coming from a fund manager. It needs a more elaborate explanation. Here we go. Reason 1: Who Are the Richest? The Ones Who Never Sell Have you looked at the Forbes list of the twenty-five wealthiest people in the world in 2022?11 In case you are interested, Elon Musk is the leader ($219 billion), and the twenty-fifth-ranked is Zhang Yiming from China ($50 billion). This list consists entirely of people who have never sold.
难道我们还未被说服吗？以进化论中复利效应的力量为背景，请允许我再列举几条我们为何应永久持有卓越企业的理由。"我永不卖出"——若出自一位充满激情的创业者之口尚可理解，但当这句话来自基金经理时，就显得有些反常（甚至有人会认为这是种谬见）。这需要更详尽的解释。请看以下分析。 理由一：谁是最富有的人？永不套现者 你可曾留意2022年《福布斯》全球富豪榜前二十五强？若你感兴趣的话，埃隆·马斯克以2190亿美元身家位居榜首，而排名第二十五位的是来自中国的张一鸣（500亿美元）。这份榜单上的所有人，无一例外都是从未抛售过核心资产的长期持有者。
26.
Even if you expand the list to the richest fifty, forty-eight are business owners (or their families) who haven’t sold. So, for example, there are two money managers—Jim Simons and Stephen Schwarzman—on the list who may buy and sell shares as a part of their fund management business. Still, they haven’t sold their businesses (Renaissance and Blackstone, respectively), which, in turn, has made them billions. If not selling is creating such humongous wealth globally, why do fund managers think they can make themselves rich by trading in and out of stocks? I know that I am not smarter or better than the richest people in the world. But if holding on to great businesses has worked wonderfully for them, why should I not simply emulate them?
即便将富豪榜名单扩大到前五十名，其中四十八位都是未出售企业的创业者（或其家族成员）。例如，榜单上仅有的两位基金经理——吉姆·西蒙斯和史蒂芬·施瓦茨曼——虽然会因基金管理业务买卖股票，但他们都未出售自己的核心资产（分别是文艺复兴科技公司和黑石集团），正是这些资产为他们创造了数百亿财富。 既然坚守企业能在全球范围内创造如此惊人的财富，为何基金经理们还认为通过频繁交易股票能致富？我深知自己不比世界上最富有的人更聪明或更优秀。但既然长期持有优质企业为他们带来了巨大成功，我为何不直接效仿呢？
27.
Many entrepreneurs on this list have had attractive offers over their lifetime. The reason for their being on the list is that they did not succumb to temptation. They intuitively understood that they were on to something quite extraordinary and that selling would have been value destroying, not value creating. For example, in 2005, Viacom offered Mark Zuckerberg $75 million for Facebook, which would have made the twenty-one-year-old a cool $35 million.12 Within a year of Viacom’s offer, Yahoo offered $1 billion for the company. Zuckerberg refused both these and many other offers. His net worth in 2022? More than $50 billion. In one way, while we may not create as much wealth as these stalwarts, we are better off than them. They are betting on just one business—their own. We have the luxury of owning many great businesses. What could be better than that? Reason 2: Empirical Evidence Shows That Owning Great Businesses Works (Oh, So Well!)
这份榜单上的许多企业家一生中都收到过诱人的收购要约。他们上榜的原因，正是从未向诱惑屈服。他们凭直觉意识到自己正参与一项非凡的事业，出售公司只会摧毁价值而非创造价值。例如2005年，维亚康姆曾出价7500万美元收购Facebook，若当时21岁的扎克伯格接受，将净赚3500万美元。而在维亚康姆报价后不到一年，雅虎又开出10亿美元的收购价。扎克伯格拒绝了这些以及后续诸多邀约。2022年他的净资产是多少？超过500亿美元。 从某种角度看，虽然我们可能无法创造这些商业巨擘般的财富，却比他们更具优势。他们仅能押注于自己的企业，而我们却能坐拥众多卓越企业。还有比这更美妙的事吗？ 理由二：实证数据证明持有卓越企业成效卓著（效果惊人！）
28.
Let’s go back to the Bessembinder study I referred to in the previous chapter.13 As a reminder, Bessembinder analyzed the price performance of 26,000 U.S.-listed stocks from 1926 to 2016. He also shares the raw data from 1926 to 2019, which is available at https://wpcarey.asu.edu/department-finance/faculty-research/do-stocks-outperform-treasury-bills. Let’s look at data from 1926 to 2019. Bessembinder defines “wealth creation” as returns earned above one-month U.S. treasuries. Of the 26,000 companies, about 60 percent (15,000) destroyed value. This is not surprising: Running a business is risky, and the data support this assertion.
让我们回顾前一章提到的贝森宾德研究。需要说明的是，贝森宾德分析了1926年至2016年间2.6万只美股的价格表现，并公开了1926至2019年的原始数据（数据详见亚利桑那州立大学金融系官网）。 以1926-2019年数据为例，贝森宾德将"财富创造"定义为超越一个月期美国国债的收益。在这2.6万家企业中，约60%（1.5万家）实际是在毁灭价值。这并不令人意外——企业经营具有风险，数据恰恰印证了这一点。
29.
But I was surprised by two facts. First, the quantum of wealth creation is almost eight times the dollar value of wealth destruction, although wealth destroyers outnumber wealth creators by almost 40 percent. About 11,000 companies created a wealth of $54 trillion, and about 15,000 businesses destroyed a wealth of $7 trillion (leading to a net wealth creation of $47 trillion). When businesses do well, the sky’s the limit. My second revelation was that only a select few companies created most of the wealth, even among the wealth creators (table 10.3). Table 10.3Wealth creation is highly concentrated in a few businesses held for longer periods No. of companies Wealth, $ trillion % of total Years held (median) Top 10% 2,617 52 110 25 Top 1% 262 35 74 47 Top 30 30 15 32 59
但我惊讶于两个事实。首先，尽管财富毁灭者的数量比财富创造者多出近40%，但财富创造的规模却是毁灭金额的八倍。约1.1万家企业创造了54万亿美元的财富，而约1.5万家企业摧毁了7万亿美元财富（最终实现47万亿美元的净财富增长）。当企业蓬勃发展时，其潜力无可限量。 我的第二个发现是，即便在财富创造者群体中，真正贡献大部分财富的也仅是少数精英企业（见表10.3）。 表10.3 财富创造高度集中于少数长期持有的企业 企业数量 创造财富（万亿美元） 占总比（%） 持有年限（中位数） 前10%企业 2,617 52 110 25 前1%企业 262 35 74 47 前30强企业 30 15 32 59
30.
Thus, the top 10 percent, or about 2,600 companies, account for all (actually, 10 percent more) of the total wealth created by the 26,000 businesses. The top 1 percent contribute to three-quarters, and just thirty firms account for almost a third of total wealth created over ninety-three years. An even more interesting finding is shown in the last column of table 10.3. A disproportionate amount of wealth is created by businesses that have been held for longer periods. That does not mean that simply holding a business for an extended period creates value—it does not; the value will almost certainly go to zero for an average business. Table 10.3 shows that if we have a great business, on average, it is likely to generate more incredible wealth over a more extended period.
因此，排名前10%（约2600家企业）创造了全部（实际超出10%）由2.6万家企业创造的财富总量。其中前1%的企业贡献了四分之三的财富，而仅仅三十家公司就占据了九十三年间创造总财富量的近三分之一。 表10.3最后一列揭示了更耐人寻味的发现：持有时间更长的企业创造了不成比例的巨额财富。但这并不意味着单纯长期持有企业就能创造价值——普通企业的价值几乎注定归零。该表表明，如果我们持有一家优秀企业，随着时间的推移，它往往能创造出更为惊人的财富。
31.
But we have one prickly issue to deal with here: How do we know what a great business is so that we can hold it for as long as possible? (I hope you did not start reading the book from this chapter—I discussed this question in chapters 1 through 7.) We do not invest in mediocre or low-quality businesses at throw-away valuations because, as table 10.3 shows, it would be a waste of time. Only a handful of companies create wealth over very long periods, and, by definition, all need to be exceptional. Instead, we invest when we believe that the business is truly outstanding, and if it is, given the stark reality of table 10.3, why would we ever sell it? I have been wrong about assessing the quality of some of our businesses. Since we hold all our businesses forever, the continuous compounding of earnings and value of a few businesses has taken care of all my follies. You want numbers? Comin’ at you. Reason 3: If There Is an Unbeatable Formula, Why Not Copy It?
但我们在此需要解决一个棘手的问题：如何判断一家卓越的企业，从而能够尽可能长期持有它？（但愿你不是直接从本章开始阅读本书——我在前七章已探讨过这个问题。）我们从不以甩卖价格投资平庸或劣质企业，因为表10.3已清楚表明，那纯粹是浪费时间。只有极少数公司能在漫长岁月中持续创造财富，而根据定义，这些公司必然都是非凡企业。相反，我们只在确信企业真正出类拔萃时才进行投资。若果真如此，面对表10.3揭示的残酷现实，我们有何理由抛售？ 我对部分企业的质量判断也曾出现失误。但由于我们永久持有所有投资，少数企业盈利与价值的持续复利增长已抵消了我所有的错误决策。需要数据佐证？马上为您呈现。 理由三：若存在必胜法则，为何不复制它？
32.
When I was at McKinsey, we addressed client problems by sharing “best practices.” These could range from advice related to post-merger integration, the process of strategy formulation, and organizational design to the allocation of marketing expenses. Of course, as a consultant, I had to account for the idiosyncrasies of a particular client. Still, I discovered that discussing “how the best businesses do it” was a great way to nudge a client toward a better solution.
在麦肯锡工作时，我们通过分享"最佳实践"来解决客户问题。这些实践涵盖并购后整合、战略制定流程、组织架构设计乃至营销费用分配等各类建议。当然，作为咨询顾问，我必须考虑每位客户的特殊性。但我发现，探讨"顶尖企业如何运作"始终是推动客户采纳更优方案的有效方式。
33.
Here is a puzzle for you to chew on. I assume you will agree that all fund managers want to earn decent returns while beating the market over the long run. Imagine a situation in which a multibillionaire investor shares his secret of getting rich with us every year in a detailed letter. His best practice is widely known and available to everyone, and it hasn’t changed for more than fifty years. We know his advice is invaluable because he continues to amass great wealth by following his teachings over almost six decades. We also know that doing what he does is not difficult to understand or even implement, at least for the professionals. But most choose to both laud him and ignore him.
这里有个值得玩味的谜题。想必你会认同：所有基金经理都希望获得可观回报，并在长期跑赢市场。试想这样一种情形——一位身价千亿的投资者每年都会通过详尽的公开信向我们分享他的致富秘诀。他的最佳实践广为人知且人人可得，五十多年来从未改变。我们知道他的建议价值连城，因为近六十年来他始终践行自己的理念并持续积累巨额财富。我们也清楚，至少对专业人士而言，效仿他的做法既不难理解，甚至也不难执行。但多数人却选择一边颂扬他，一边忽视他。
34.
That investor, of course, is Warren Buffett, and his simple advice to buy exceptional businesses at a sensible price and hold them forever has made him one of the wealthiest people in the world. So then why does his advice fall on deaf ears? At first glance, this seems somewhat bizarre. Investors seem to be voluntarily giving up the chance to get rich. But if you think about it for a moment, you will realize that Buffett’s advice is hard to fathom for the same reason that Darwin’s insight was not accepted for many decades. We humans don’t understand compounding. We say we do, but we don’t.
这位投资者正是沃伦·巴菲特。他"以合理价格买入卓越企业并永久持有"的朴素建议，使其跻身世界顶级富豪之列。但为何世人对此忠告充耳不闻？初看之下着实费解——投资者似乎自愿放弃了致富良机。但细想便会明白，正如达尔文的真知灼见沉寂数十年才被接纳，巴菲特箴言难被领悟的根源在于：人类从未真正理解复利。我们自以为懂得，实则不然。
35.
Buffett is the Darwin of investing—he changed the field forever and for the better. But if eminent scientists in the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries could barely comprehend the power of cumulative growth, how can investors, who by and large are much more intellectually challenged, be expected to appreciate it? But the problem is worse than you think. Not only do investors blithely ignore Buffett, their behavior over the last fifty years indicates that they firmly believe the exact opposite! The holding period of stocks by mutual funds has fallen to less than a year from seven years in 1960. Let’s return to Shelby Cullom Davis. Despite being radically different from Buffett in almost every way, how did he create his wealth? Just like Buffett, Davis held on to a select few quality businesses for decades.
巴菲特是投资界的达尔文——他彻底改变了这个领域，并使其变得更好。但如果说十九世纪末二十世纪初的杰出科学家都难以理解复利增长的力量，那么整体认知水平更低的投资者们又怎能领会其精髓？问题比想象的更严重。投资者不仅对巴菲特的理念置若罔闻，过去五十年的行为数据更表明他们坚信完全相反的法则！共同基金持有股票的平均周期已从1960年的七年缩短至不足一年。 让我们回到谢尔比·库洛姆·戴维斯。这位与巴菲特几乎处处迥异的人物，如何缔造了他的财富帝国？答案与巴菲特如出一辙：数十年如一日地坚守少数优质企业。
36.
Unlike Buffett, who always wanted to be an investor, Davis became an investor through a series of fortunate events. When he got married in January 1932, the Dow hit an all-time low of 41—it had fallen 89 percent from its peak in 1929. His wife, Kathryn, provided him his seed money for investing many years later; Davis was lucky that Kathryn’s father, Joseph Wasserman, had kept his money in government bonds and lost nothing in the Crash.
与自幼立志成为投资家的巴菲特不同，戴维斯成为投资者纯属机缘巧合。1932年1月他结婚时，道琼斯指数跌至41点的历史新低——较1929年峰值暴跌89%。多年后，他的妻子凯瑟琳为他提供了投资启动资金；戴维斯很幸运，因为凯瑟琳的父亲约瑟夫·瓦瑟曼将资产全部配置为政府债券，在大萧条中毫发未损。
37.
After working as a reporter for CBS Radio, Davis earned his PhD along with Kathryn in political science at the University of Geneva (where Kathryn outscored him). In 1934, Davis was offered a job in Tokyo at the English-language newspaper, the Advertiser. Just as he and Kathryn were about to depart for Japan, an earthquake hit Tokyo, forcing them to cancel their trip. Also, the Advertiser offer fell through. Davis was now desperate for a job, but he could not find any employment in journalism in the sickening state of the U.S. economy. Kathryn asked her brother, Bill, to employ Davis in his investment firm.
戴维斯曾在哥伦比亚广播公司电台担任记者，后与凯瑟琳一同在日内瓦大学获得政治学博士学位（凯瑟琳的成绩比他更优异）。1934年，东京英文报纸《广告报》向戴维斯提供了一份工作。就在他和凯瑟琳即将启程前往日本时，东京发生地震，迫使两人取消行程。与此同时，《广告报》的职位也落空了。当时美国经济萎靡不振，戴维斯虽迫切求职，却无法在新闻行业找到任何工作。凯瑟琳便请求兄长比尔让戴维斯进入其投资公司任职。
38.
Davis worked as a “statistician” in Bill’s firm and traveled around the country meeting companies that looked promising for investment. But Davis and Bill did not get along, and Davis left the job to start writing full time. He published a book called America Faces the Forties, which explored the causes of the Great Depression and how the 1940s might lead to recovery. It was reasonably well received and caught the eye of Thomas E. Dewey, the governor of New York and Republican presidential hopeful (he lost to Roosevelt in 1944 and to Truman in 1948). In 1938, Dewey made Davis his speechwriter and economic adviser.
戴维斯在比尔的公司担任"统计员"，走遍全国考察有投资潜力的企业。但戴维斯与比尔相处不睦，遂离职专职写作。他出版了《美国面对四十年代》一书，探讨大萧条的成因及1940年代经济复苏的可能路径。该书反响尚可，引起了纽约州长、共和党总统候选人托马斯·杜威的注意（此人1944年败于罗斯福，1948年又输给杜鲁门）。1938年，杜威聘请戴维斯担任演讲稿撰写人兼经济顾问。
39.
After losing to Roosevelt in 1944, Dewey returned to his role as the governor of New York. He unknowingly put Davis on the path to fabulous riches by appointing him the deputy superintendent of the state’s insurance department. Could there be a more boring-sounding job? But Davis took it seriously. He was an outspoken advocate of insurance companies diversifying from bonds to real estate, mortgages, and stocks. Contrary to popular opinion in those days, Davis considered bonds extremely risky. Nevertheless, he was remarkably prescient. Bonds went into a thirty-five-year bear market from the mid-1940s; the government bond sold for $101 in 1946 sold for just $17 in 1981.
1944年败给罗斯福后，杜威重回纽约州长之位。他任命戴维斯为州保险厅副厅长，这一无心之举却为后者铺就了致富坦途。世上还有比这头衔更乏味的职位吗？但戴维斯却全力以赴。他公开主张保险公司不应只投资债券，而应涉足房地产、抵押贷款和股票。与当时主流观点相反，他认为债券风险极高。这番远见卓识令人叹服——债券市场自1940年代中期开启了长达35年的熊市，1946年价值101美元的政府债券，到1981年竟暴跌至17美元。
40.
Investors ignored insurance companies, usually quoted in the minor league of stock exchanges. Insurers were required to file their latest financials with the state agency, and Davis pored over these reports, becoming an expert at understanding their inner workings. He discovered that a typical insurer was selling for less than its “true” book value—just the bonds and mortgages in an insurer’s portfolio could be worth far more than its market value. He realized that insurance customers paid money up front and that insurers could deploy this “float” to buy bonds and mortgages. If customer claims weren’t excessive, this hidden float could slowly and silently balloon over time. A patient investor could wait for this hidden asset to compound until the market, too, recognized it.
投资者对保险公司不屑一顾，这类股票通常被视为交易所的次要品种。由于保险公司需向州政府机构提交最新财务报告，戴维斯便潜心研读这些文件，逐渐成为洞悉其内部运作的专家。他发现，典型保险公司的股价往往低于其"真实"账面价值——仅保险公司投资组合中的债券和抵押贷款价值，就可能远超其市值。他意识到，保险客户会预先支付保费，而保险公司可将这笔"浮存金"用于投资债券和抵押贷款。只要客户索赔不过度，这笔隐性浮存金就能随时间悄然膨胀。有耐心的投资者可以等待这项隐性资产持续增值，直到市场最终发现其价值。
41.
Davis left his job in 1947, borrowed $50,000 from Kathryn, and started investing in well-run and dividend-paying insurance companies selling for less than their book value. He also borrowed on the margin to fund some of his purchases. In a speech to the New York Insurance Brokers Association in 1952, Davis outlined his three criteria for selecting the stock of an insurer: (1) The insurer had to be profitable, (2) its assets (bonds, mortgages, stocks) needed to be of the highest quality, and (3) its market price had to be lower than its private market value. Davis was a value investor in high-quality insurers. And he held on to them.
戴维斯于1947年辞去工作，向凯瑟琳借了5万美元，开始投资于运营良好、支付股息且股价低于账面价值的保险公司。他还通过保证金贷款为部分购买提供资金。在1952年纽约保险经纪人协会的一次演讲中，戴维斯概述了他选择保险公司股票的三项标准：（1）保险公司必须盈利；（2）其资产（债券、抵押贷款、股票）必须具有最高质量；（3）其市场价格必须低于其私有市场价值。戴维斯是一位专注于高质量保险公司的价值投资者。而且他长期持有这些股票。
42.
In 1992, two years before his death, his top twelve holdings were worth $261 million—about half his total portfolio. Except for Fannie Mae, all were insurance companies. And he had bought each decades ago. His best investment, worth $72 million, was AIG, and his third-best, worth $27 million, was Berkshire Hathaway. Once he bought a great business, he never sold it. Why should we reinvent the wheel when we have spectacular successes like Buffett and Davis to emulate? As I will discuss, Davis’s success shows that we don’t even have to be that good to succeed. Just patient. And so we are. Reason 4: How Else Do I Pay for My Mistakes? Shelby Davis bought about a hundred insurers that made up three-quarters of his portfolio, and about 1,500 companies globally made up the rest. Most of these investments turned out to be duds! His other big mistake was to buy junk bonds worth about $23 million—almost all turned out to be actual junk.
1992年，也就是谢尔比·戴维斯去世前两年，他持仓前十二名的股票总值达2.61亿美元，约占其投资组合的一半。除房利美外，其余全是保险公司——且都是他数十年前买入的。其中表现最佳的是价值7200万美元的美国国际集团，排名第三的是价值2700万美元的伯克希尔·哈撒韦。他一旦买入优质企业，便永不脱手。 既然有巴菲特和戴维斯这样卓越的成功典范可供效仿，我们何必另辟蹊径？正如后文将探讨的，戴维斯的成功证明我们甚至无需天赋异禀——只需保持耐心。而这正是我们具备的品质。 理由四：如何为错误买单？ 戴维斯持仓中约四分之三由百余家保险公司构成，其余则分散于全球约1500家企业。其中多数投资最终沦为败笔！他另一个重大失误是购入了价值约2300万美元的垃圾债券——后来这些债券几乎全都名副其实地成了废纸。
43.
Davis made all his wealth by investing in a few high-quality insurers and then refusing to sell them. As a result, his hundreds of mistakes became irrelevant in the context of the exceptional long-term compounding of his winners. In his book The Davis Dynasty, John Rothchild states this eloquently: “In the final analysis, Davis’s mistakes hindered his prosperity the way a gnat flusters a buffalo. Nevertheless, his portfolio proved once again that, over a lifetime of investing, a handful of high achievers’ ideas could support a multitude of ne’er-do-wells.” I have made many mistakes, and I know I will continue to do so. This is not humility but a cold hard fact. Waiting for a few great businesses to compound has paid for these mistakes. Let me share the actual numbers with you.
戴维斯的所有财富都来自对少数优质保险公司的投资并长期持有。正因如此，在那些赢家标的的长期惊人复利面前，他数百次失误都变得无足轻重。约翰·罗斯柴尔德在《戴维斯王朝》一书中精辟总结道："归根结底，戴维斯的失误对他财富增长的影响，就像蚊虫对水牛的骚扰般微不足道。但他的投资组合再次证明：在漫长的投资生涯中，少数卓越标的创造的收益，足以抵消无数失败决策的损失。" 我犯过许多错误，也清楚未来仍会重蹈覆辙。这并非谦辞，而是冰冷的事实。但等待少数杰出企业持续创造复利，足以弥补所有这些失误。让我用真实数据为你说明。
44.
Our first fund invested about INR 18 billion (about $400 million using the exchange rate prevalent at the time) in seventeen businesses from June 2007 to June 2011. In June 2022, given that enough time had passed, we could reliably assess the share price performance of individual companies in this fund. We had only one capital loss in the portfolio, so that was a failure. Let me arbitrarily label any business (or rather, the market value of the business) earning an annualized rupee return of less than 10 percent a “failure” as well. Six of the seventeen businesses had earned an annualized rupee return of less than 10 percent by June 2022. Thus, we had seven failures (one loss and six with an annualized return of less than 10 percent) out of seventeen businesses, or a “failure” rate of 40 percent.
我们的首支基金在2007年6月至2011年6月期间，向17家企业投资了约180亿印度卢比（按当时汇率计算约合4亿美元）。截至2022年6月，经过足够长的时间跨度，我们得以准确评估该基金持仓企业的股价表现。投资组合中仅出现一例本金亏损，这显然属于失败案例。在此我将年化卢比收益率低于10%的企业（更准确说是企业市值）也武断地归类为"失败"。到2022年6月，17家企业中有6家的年化卢比收益率低于10%。因此，17笔投资中共出现7例失败（1例本金亏损加6例年化收益不足10%），失败率达40%。
45.
But the overall performance of this fund has been better than my wildest dreams. So how did we get here given the underperformance of seven of our businesses? Because we did not sell our winners. Let me call these seven “failed” businesses the “Sorry Seven.” We invested INR 7.8 billion in the Sorry Seven. Let’s see what happens when we hold a good business for a long time. Take Supreme, India’s leading plastic products company. We invested in Supreme in 2010, and by June 2022, we had owned it for almost twelve years. We invested INR 1 billion in Supreme, which was worth INR 13.9 billion in June 2022. The gain of INR 12.9 billion in Supreme is 1.7 times the total amount invested in the Sorry Seven (12.9 ÷ 7.8 = 1.7). But it’s much better than that. By June 2022, six investments had individually paid for the total amount invested in the Sorry Seven. Table 10.4 lists what I call the “Superb Six.” Table 10.4Long-term winners pay for the losers many times over (as of June 30, 2022 [in INR])
但这只基金的整体表现远超我最狂野的预期。既然七项投资都表现不佳，我们为何还能取得这样的成绩？因为我们没有抛售赢家。 请允许我将这七个"失败"项目称为"遗憾七人组"。我们在它们身上共计投入了78亿卢比。现在让我们看看长期持有优质企业的结果——以印度塑料制品行业龙头Supreme公司为例。我们于2010年投资Supreme，截至2022年6月已持有近十二年。当初10亿卢比的投资，到2022年6月已增值至139亿卢比。仅Supreme带来的129亿卢比收益，就是"遗憾七人组"总投资的1.7倍（129÷78=1.7）。 实际情况更为乐观。截至2022年6月，已有六项投资的单项收益完全覆盖了"遗憾七人组"的总投入。表10.4呈现了我称之为"卓越六君子"的投资组合。 表10.4 长期赢家多次覆盖失败投资成本（截至2022年6月30日[单位：卢比]）
46.
Company No. of years held Multiple Gain ÷ total investment in the Sorry Seven Berger 13.3 32.2× 3.3 Mindtree 9.6 8.2× 1.7 Page 13.7 82.2× 5.2 Ratnamani 11.7 16.2× 1.0 Supreme 11.6 13.6× 1.7 WNS 13 10.6× 3.2 It’s almost ridiculous, isn’t it? Simply owning Page for fourteen years compensated for seven unsuccessful investments more than five times over. If the upside of holding companies for long periods is so significant, why don’t investors do it? One critical reason is an underappreciation of compounding, which makes fund managers value IRR more than the multiple, instead of the other way around.
公司名称 持有年限（年） 回报倍数 收益÷"遗憾七股"总投资额 Berger公司 13.3 32.2倍 3.3 Mindtree公司 9.6 8.2倍 1.7 Page公司 13.7 82.2倍 5.2 Ratnamani公司 11.7 16.2倍 1.0 Supreme公司 11.6 13.6倍 1.7 WNS公司 13 10.6倍 3.2 这简直荒谬，不是吗？仅仅持有Page公司十四年，其收益就足以弥补七项失败投资损失的5倍有余。既然长期持股的收益如此可观，为何投资者鲜少为之？关键在于人们低估了复利效应——这使得基金经理更重视内部收益率而非回报倍数，实则应反其道而行。
47.
In finance jargon, IRR is the internal rate of return, or the annualized rate of return. If a stock doubles in four years, its IRR is 19 percent, and if it doubles in three, its IRR is 26 percent. For the same multiple, the shorter the period, the higher the IRR. Ignoring the beauty of compounding, investors like to boast about the IRR of their investment while undervaluing the benefits of the multiple.
用金融术语来说，IRR即内部收益率，也就是年化回报率。若一只股票四年内翻倍，其内部收益率为19%；若三年翻倍，收益率则为26%。在相同倍数下，周期越短，收益率越高。投资者常沉迷于吹捧投资收益率，却忽视了倍数增长的魅力，未能充分认识到复利的价值。
48.
If we had been fans of IRR, we would have sold each of the Superb Six listed in table 10.4 a long time ago. The colossal downside of doing this is evident from the example of Page. In December 2012, after four years of our owning Page, it had delivered 65 percent IRR (!). For most investors, a holding period of four years seems long enough. It would not have been very intelligent to think that we could earn 65 percent IRR incrementally over the next five to ten years. If we were IRR fans, we would have exited Page in December 2012, crowed about the astronomical return delivered over four years, and described the return in bold in our marketing materials (actually, we don’t have any marketing materials, but that is beside the point).
若我们真是内部收益率（IRR）的拥趸，恐怕早就抛售表10.4所列的"卓越六杰"了。这种做法可能造成的巨大损失，从佩奇公司的例子可见一斑。2012年12月，在我们持有佩奇四年后，其IRR已达到惊人的65%。对多数投资者而言，四年持有期已足够漫长。若认为未来五到十年还能在此基础上继续获得65%的IRR，显然不够明智。倘若我们迷信IRR，本应在2012年12月就清仓佩奇，在营销材料中用加粗字体大肆宣扬这四年创造的"天文数字"回报（当然我们从不制作营销材料，不过这并非重点）。
49.
The multiple on Page in December 2012 was 7.8× (compared to 82.2× in June 2022), so the gain on investment was “only” INR 3.4 billion. Remember that the cost of investment in the Sorry Seven of INR 7.8 billion does not change, regardless of the holding period of Page. Thus, if we had sold Page in December 2012, we would have recouped only 44 percent (3.4 ÷ 7.8 = 44 percent) of our investment in the Sorry Seven. The remaining 56 percent burden would have had to be carried by the remaining businesses. However, since we have continued to hold Page, our gain has climbed to INR 40.8 billion, and the Sorry Seven have been paid for 5.2 times over by the gain of this single holding (40.8 ÷ 7.8 = 5.2).
2012年12月Page的市盈率为7.8倍（2022年6月为82.2倍），因此投资收益"仅"为34亿卢比。需注意，无论持有Page多久，对"遗憾七子"78亿卢比的投资成本都不会改变。若我们在2012年12月出售Page，仅能收回对"遗憾七子"总投资的44%（3.4÷7.8=44%），剩余56%的亏损仍需由其他业务承担。但由于我们持续持有Page，当前收益已攀升至408亿卢比，仅这一项投资的盈利就足以覆盖"遗憾七子"投资成本的5.2倍（40.8÷7.8=5.2）。
50.
Remember the example of the rare mutant with color vision (just eight in one thousand) with only a 1 percent selective advantage that overwhelmed the population in three thousand generations? Only a handful of compounders in a portfolio, growing a little more than the rest, achieve the same result given enough time. We invest only in what we think are phenomenal businesses. But I also know that some may not perform and will need to be paid for. Hence, for investors like us, even thinking of selling our winners is worse than wrong. It’s foolish. Reason 5: The Only Way to Benefit from Compounding Is to Stay Invested If we are aggressive buyers during adverse stock price movements, logic dictates that we should be aggressive sellers when stock prices rise suddenly. But, thankfully, some of the essential things in life—believing our children are unique, falling in love, being a dedicated doctor or nurse during the COVID-19 pandemic, volunteering to be a soldier—are not driven by logic.
还记得那个关于罕见色觉突变体的例子吗？（每千人中仅有八例）仅凭1%的选择优势，它就在三千代后席卷了整个种群。投资组合中只需少数几家复合增长型企业，假以时日，它们略高于平均的增速就能产生同样的效果。 我们只投资于非凡的企业。但我也清楚，有些企业可能表现不佳，需要其他投资来弥补。因此，对我们这类投资者而言，考虑卖出赢家股不仅是错误，更是愚蠢之举。 第五条：享受复利红利的唯一方式是长期持有 若我们在股价下跌时大举买入，按照逻辑就该在股价暴涨时大举抛售。但值得庆幸的是，生命中某些重要之事——坚信子女独一无二、坠入爱河、在新冠疫情期间坚守医者岗位、志愿从军——本就不受逻辑驱使。
51.
We don’t sell when stock prices rise suddenly. These nonactions during market euphoria have been as important as—actually, more important than—our acts of buying during market panics. As I wrote earlier, as of June 2022, out of our portfolio of twenty-four businesses (excluding the ones bought during the previous two years), we had multiplied our money by more than ten times in INR in nine (of these, the largest multiple, 82×, was for Page, and the smallest, 13×, was for Info Edge). In five of these nine, our holding period had been more than eleven years, and we had held the remaining ten-baggers for more than eight years. Why do we not sell when stock prices rise dramatically? The answer is shown in table 10.5. Here, I have selected two of the nine businesses whose values have multiplied by more than ten times in INR. Table 10.5The prodigious power of positive punctuations (June 2007 to June 2022) Measure Havells Page Holding period Years 8.5 13.7 Trading days 2,724 3,586 Total gain
我们不会在股价突然上涨时抛售。在市场狂热时期保持按兵不动的重要性，实际上更甚于我们在市场恐慌时期的买入行为。正如我之前所述，截至2022年6月，在我们持有的24家企业投资组合中（不含过去两年新购入的企业），有9家企业的投资回报以印度卢比计算超过了十倍（其中最高回报82倍来自Page公司，最低13倍来自Info Edge公司）。这9家企业中有5家的持有期超过11年，其余实现十倍回报的企业持有期均超过8年。 为何我们不在股价暴涨时卖出？ 答案展现在表10.5中。这里我选取了9家企业中2家以印度卢比计算价值增长超十倍的企业作为示例。 表10.5 正向间断的惊人威力（2007年6月至2022年6月） 指标 Havells Page 持有年限 8.5 13.7 交易日数 2,724 3,586 总收益
52.

The latter tracks the increase in stock price, whereas the former shows the appreciation of the values of our holdings. The values are marginally different because table 10.4 accounts for redemptions in the fund (which force us to sell all stocks in proportion to their value). The difference, as you can see, is very small. Let me explain what you see in Havells. As of June 2022, we had held Havells for 8.5 years, or 2,724 days of trading (not counting holidays).
