53.
• 90 percent of the gain of 1,270 percent came in just thirty-five days. Those thirty-five days account for only 1.3 percent of the total number of trading days during which we held Havells. What if we had sold Havells during one (or more) of those very few days? Those thirty-five days are distributed across all years. For example, the top three gains for the stock came on September 20, 2019; January 21, 2021; and June 5, 2014. If, excited by the sudden price rise, we had sold our shares on June 5, 2014, we would have missed the significant jumps on September 20, 2019, and January 21, 2021. As you can see, the numbers for Page are similar: 90 percent of the total gains came in just 2 percent of trading days.
1,270%的总涨幅中，90%的收益仅来自35个交易日。这35天仅占我们持有哈维尔股票期间总交易天数的1.3%。倘若我们在其中少数几个关键交易日卖出会如何？这些决定性的日子分散在不同年份——例如该股涨幅最大的三天分别出现在2019年9月20日、2021年1月21日和2014年6月5日。若因2014年6月5日的股价飙升而兴奋抛售，我们将错失2019年与2021年那两次重大飞跃。佩吉公司的数据同样印证这点：90%的总收益来自仅占2%的交易天数。
54.
• Havells stock gained 5 percent or more on just forty-four days, or 1.6 percent of the total number of trading days during our holding period. If we add up the gains from those days, they sum to 1,800 percent, or 142 percent of the total gains over 8.5 years. Thus, the forty-four days of stock price gains of 5 percent or more accounted for more than the total gain during our entire holding period of almost nine years! The opportunity cost of not holding on to Havells shares during those significant days would have been egregiously high. Check out the astronomical impact of 5-percent-plus days in Page—they accounted for more than 300 percent of total gains! It would have been impossible for us to compound our capital if we had not remained invested in Page.
哈维尔斯的股票在我们持股期间仅有44个交易日（占总交易日数的1.6%）实现了5%或以上的涨幅。若将这些交易日的涨幅累加，总和达到1,800%，相当于8.5年总收益的142%。也就是说，这44个涨幅超5%的交易日贡献的收益，甚至超过了近九年持股期的全部收益总和！若在这些关键交易日未能持有哈维尔斯股票，机会成本将极其高昂。再看佩吉公司——涨幅超5%的交易日贡献了总收益的300%以上！若未持续投资佩吉公司，我们根本不可能实现资本复利增长。
55.
• Last, please look at the data from the gloomy days (i.e., days when the stock price declined). I was pretty surprised to see that the negative days account for almost half the total number of trading days across all three businesses. But, as you can see, the negative days didn’t matter because we held on to the companies throughout this period. Do you see where I am going with this analysis? If we had sold Havells or our other compounders on any day when their stock prices rose significantly, we would have been celebrated for raking in cash. Still, we would have repented at leisure as the stock prices continued to rise over the long run.
最后，请观察股价下跌时期的交易数据。我惊讶地发现，这三家企业的股价下跌天数几乎都占到总交易天数的一半。但正如所见，这些下跌无关紧要，因为我们始终持有这些公司的股票。 明白我的分析指向何处了吗？如果我们在哈维尔或其他优质企业的股价大涨当天选择抛售，短期内套现的举动或许会赢得喝彩。但从长期来看，随着股价持续攀升，我们终将在闲适之时追悔莫及。
56.
But how did I know that the Havells stock price would continue to rise? I didn’t because I cannot predict stock prices. I can make two predictions, though. First, if we own a high-quality business, the share price will most probably (but not assuredly) react positively over the long run. Second, the share price will rarely make big moves, and if I am not invested in the stock on those particular days, I can bid farewell to substantial potential gains. If we have done anything right, we have not done anything on days when selling seems to be the most logical thing to do. Reason 6: I Love Our Entrepreneurs I love our entrepreneurs. Behavioral economists have a quaint name for this disease: the endowment effect. It is the irrational mindset that assigns a disproportionately high value to what one owns.
但我如何确信哈维尔股价会持续上涨？其实我并不知道，因为我无法预测股价走势。不过我可以做出两个预判：首先，若我们持有优质企业，长期来看股价极可能（虽非绝对）呈现积极反应；其次，股价鲜少出现大幅波动，若恰逢这些关键交易日我未持股，便可能与巨额潜在收益失之交臂。 若说我们有何成功之处，那就是在看似最该抛售的交易日里，我们选择了按兵不动。 理由六：我钟爱我们的企业家 我深爱我们的企业家。行为经济学家给这种情结起了个雅号：禀赋效应。这种非理性心态会让人对自己拥有的事物赋予过高价值。
57.
Investing is supposed to be a cut-and-dried profession where, à la Mr. Spock, fund managers dispassionately enter and exit businesses based on intellect, instinct, or insight. Unfortunately, we fulfill this requirement only for entry and some exits. Before investing, we base our decision entirely on empirical evidence, as I have shown in chapters 1 through 7. But after we have invested, and if a business continues to do well, I become emotionally attached to it. India is a tough place to do business (I am sure all countries are, but India is the only market I know), and almost every industry is fiercely competitive. In this cutthroat marketplace, any entrepreneur who stays ahead of the competition by taking calculated risks while maintaining high profitability and a clean balance sheet is genuinely admirable.
投资本该是个干脆利落的行当——就像斯波克先生那样，基金经理们凭借理性、直觉或洞见，冷静地买入和卖出企业。可惜我们只做到了冷静买入和部分卖出。 如我在前七章所述，投资决策完全基于实证分析。但一旦完成投资，若企业持续表现良好，我就会产生情感依赖。印度是个营商环境严苛的国度（想必各国皆如此，但印度是我唯一熟悉的市场），几乎所有行业都竞争惨烈。在这片红海市场中，那些通过精准冒险持续保持领先地位，同时维持高盈利与健康资产负债表的企业家，实在令人钦佩。
58.
I know that new-age technology companies are in vogue, and everyone in the world seems to laud them while they blow other people’s money by the millions or billions. (Where’s the glory in selling a dollar for eighty cents? Maybe I am getting too old.) In sharp contrast to these cash-guzzling sinkholes, take the cases of Ahluwalia, DB Corp, Triveni Turbine, and Voltamp, four companies in our portfolio that are leaders in their field. Like clockwork, they throw up significantly more cash than they consume every year. However, our investment in them has yielded subpar returns for a decade or more. My fault, not theirs. Part of the reason for continuing to own them is that we hope the tide will turn over time (as it has for many of our other businesses). Still, an important motivation is also that I love the leaders of these businesses. They are genuinely outstanding, as shown by their operating and financial track records over many decades.
我深知新时代科技公司正风靡一时，当它们挥霍他人数百万乃至数十亿资金时，全球似乎都在为之喝彩。（以八毛钱价格卖一块钱的东西，荣耀何在？或许是我太老派了。）与这些吞噬现金的无底洞形成鲜明对比的，是我们投资组合中的四家行业领军企业：Ahluwalia、DB Corp、Triveni Turbine和Voltamp。这些企业如同精密钟表般，每年创造的现金流远超其消耗量。然而我们对它们的投资却在十年乃至更长时间里表现平平。这是我的失误，而非企业之过。我们持续持有的部分原因，是期待转机终将到来（正如我们其他许多投资曾经历的那样）。但更重要的动力在于，我由衷欣赏这些企业的掌舵人。数十年的经营与财务业绩证明，他们确实是出类拔萃的领导者。
59.
One of the great pleasures of our profession is that we get to know and build relationships with the likes of Shobhit Uppal, Sudhir Agarwal, Dhruv Sawhney, and K. S. Patel. I am in awe of them. So why should I give up this gratification for a few dollars? Reason 7: Not Selling Makes Us Better Buyers That seems like a weird assertion. How can not selling cause better buying? Here is how. How much time do you think fund managers devote to thinking about the “right” sale price for their businesses? If you manage money, you already know the answer, but if you aren’t a fund manager, please ask someone who is. The answer will probably range from 30 to 70 percent. Some fund managers argue, “If we are not a buyer, we are a seller.” These people are probably contemplating a sale all the time.
我们这一行最大的乐趣之一，就是能结识肖布希特·乌帕尔、苏迪尔·阿加瓦尔、德鲁夫·索内和K·S·帕特尔这样的人并与之建立情谊。我对他们心怀敬仰。既然如此，我又怎会为区区金钱放弃这份满足？ 第七个理由：拒绝出售让我们成为更明智的买家 这个说法看似奇怪。不卖怎么会促成更好的买？且听分解。 你认为基金经理会花多少时间思考自己企业的"合理"出售价格？若是资管从业者自然心知肚明，若非业内人士，不妨找位基金经理问问。答案多半在30%到70%之间。有些基金经理主张："我们不买即卖。"这些人恐怕无时无刻不在考虑出售事宜。
60.
Let’s say we want to figure out whether we should exit Ratnamani, one of our portfolio companies and India’s most significant specialty steel business. Ratnamani’s clients are primarily refineries and petrochemical plants, both of which are cyclical industries. Hence, Ratnamani’s revenues and profits, too, are cyclical. We first need to decide upon a time frame over which we will calculate the incremental return. It could be one year, three years, or five years, or some other period. At the end of that time frame, we will need to forecast Ratnamani’s profits and valuation multiple (PE, EV/EBITDA, or some other metric).
假设我们需要决定是否应该退出投资组合公司Ratnamani——印度最重要的特种钢企业。该公司的客户主要是炼油厂和石化工厂，这两个行业都具有周期性特征。因此，Ratnamani的营收与利润同样呈现周期性波动。 我们首先需要确定计算增量回报的时间范围，可以是一年、三年、五年或其他周期。在该时间段结束时，我们需要预测Ratnamani的利润水平及估值倍数（市盈率、企业价值倍数或其他指标）。
61.
If we want to calculate a three-year incremental return, we will need to forecast Ratnamani’s revenues, expenses, and tax rates for the next three years. This is a nontrivial exercise for a cyclical business. First, a hapless analyst in the organization will need to trash their weekends to collate the capital expenditure announcements of all the refineries and petrochemical plants that could be Ratnamani’s clients. Next, they will need to assume a particular market share for Ratnamani to forecast the company revenue. (“How?” you ask? I have no idea—ask the analyst.) Finally, they will conduct a similarly detailed exercise for the significant expense lines: depreciation, raw material, employees, sales and general administration, and taxes, to name just a few. And let’s not even discuss the myriad ways of projecting a valuation multiple three years from now.
若要计算三年期增量回报，我们需要预测拉特纳米公司未来三年的收入、支出及税率。这对周期性企业而言并非易事。首先，公司里某个倒霉的分析师将不得不牺牲周末时间，汇总所有可能成为拉特纳米客户的炼油厂与石化厂的资本支出公告。接着，他们需假设拉特纳米能获得特定市场份额，以此推算公司收入。（"具体怎么做？"你问？我也不清楚——去问那位分析师吧。）最后，他们还需对主要支出项——包括折旧、原材料、员工薪酬、销售及行政管理费用、税费等——进行同样细致的测算。至于如何预测三年后的估值倍数？那更是不胜枚举的方法了。
62.
Some asset managers may not resort to such a detailed exercise; they may choose to sell if the multiple or the stock price reaches a certain level. But even these professionals will need to keep track of the businesses that approach the sale price and debate whether their initial assumptions are still valid (e.g., what if the company’s main competitor is in trouble?). All this takes time, energy, and, most importantly, mind space. We do no such analyses. We buy never to sell. None of our professionals spends even a minute thinking about selling unless the business makes an egregiously wrong capital allocation or if the company (according to us) is irreparably damaged.
部分资产管理人可能不会进行如此细致的分析——当市盈率或股价达到特定水平时，他们就会选择抛售。但即便是这些专业人士，也需要持续追踪那些逼近抛售价位的标的，并反复验证最初的投资假设是否依然成立（例如：若该公司的主要竞争对手陷入困境会怎样？）。 这些行为不仅耗费时间和精力，更重要的是挤占心智空间。我们从不进行此类分析。我们的买入决策以永久持有为前提。除非企业出现严重的资本配置失误，或我们认为该公司已遭受不可逆转的损害，否则我们的专业团队连一分钟都不会浪费在思考卖出问题上。
63.
In the last chapter, in table 9.2, I showed you the three occasions—the 2008 financial crisis, the 2011 Euro crisis (the sovereign debt crisis in Europe that began in 2009 led to the change or collapse of the majority of euro zone governments from March 2011 to May 2012),15 and the COVID-19 pandemic—when we were highly aggressive buyers. Given that we were inactive for many years, what allowed us to buy stocks worth $288 million (16 percent of the total amount invested since our inception in 2007) in just seventeen days in March 2020? We acted decisively and disruptively because we were well prepared. We are always well prepared to buy because we have been freed of the concerns of selling. Just because I have time to think does not mean I will think correctly; I have made buying mistakes and will continue to do so. But freed from the worries of selling, our buying process is highly focused and disciplined. What more can I ask? “It Does Not Make Any Sense”
在上一章的表格9.2中，我向您展示了我们三次大规模买入的时机——2008年金融危机、2011年欧债危机（2009年爆发的欧洲主权债务危机导致2011年3月至2012年5月期间欧元区多数政府更迭或垮台）以及新冠疫情。考虑到我们多年按兵不动，为何能在2020年3月短短十七天内斥资2.88亿美元（占2007年成立以来总投资额的16%）买入股票？我们之所以能果断颠覆性出击，是因为准备充分。我们始终做好买入准备，只因无需担忧抛售问题。 拥有思考时间并不等同于正确思考；我曾犯下买入错误，未来也难免重蹈覆辙。但摆脱了抛售的顾虑，我们的买入流程便高度专注且纪律严明。夫复何求？ "这毫无道理"
64.
It seems too easy, isn’t it? Buy a great business. Sit tight. Watch the moolah roll in. It is, and it is not. Over my decades of investing, I have heard many objections from my fund manager friends and investors who have refused to give us money because they were uncomfortable with our permanent owner approach. “It does not make sense” is a common refrain after I reveal that we plan to be permanent owners. Let me share with you some of these objections and my responses to them. Objection 1: Why Should I Hold On to 60 PE? We are price sensitive; we do not invest if the valuation is high. A logical question, then, is, Why aren’t we sellers when the valuation is high?
听起来太简单了，不是吗？买下一家优秀企业，牢牢握住，坐等财富滚滚而来。 事情既是如此，又并非如此。在我数十年的投资生涯中，听过太多基金经理朋友和投资者的反对意见——他们因不认同我们"永久持有"的理念而拒绝投资。每当我透露打算永久持有时，"这不合常理"成了最常听到的回应。 请允许我分享几条典型质疑及我的答复。 质疑一：为何要坚守60倍市盈率？ 我们向来注重价格，估值过高时绝不投资。那么合乎逻辑的疑问是：为何不在高估值时抛售？
65.
Take a concrete example of a business that went from a PE multiple of 15× to a PE multiple of 60× over five years of our holding period. Let’s say that earnings doubled during those five years. We would be sitting on a multiple of eight times our initial investment: four times from multiple expansion and two times from earnings growth. Many investors would justify selling at this point with the following calculation. Let’s say the business doubles its earnings over the next five years (the same as over the last five years). If the PE multiple stays the same, we will only double our money, and if it halves to 30 PE (which is possible because the long-term market PE is 19 to 20), we will not make any return for the next five years. So shouldn’t we be sellers? It’s a logical and fair question. It is so logical and fair that most fund managers will sell and exit at this point. We won’t. The reasons are three-fold.
举个具体例子：某企业在我们持有的五年间，市盈率从15倍升至60倍。假设这五年间企业盈利翻倍，我们的初始投资将增值至八倍——其中四倍来自市盈率扩张，两倍来自盈利增长。 此时许多投资者会这样计算并选择卖出：假设该企业未来五年盈利再次翻倍（与过去五年持平），若市盈率保持不变，我们仅能实现本金翻倍；若市盈率回落至30倍（考虑到长期市场市盈率为19-20倍，这完全可能），未来五年将毫无收益。那么现在是否应该卖出？ 这是个合理且公正的质疑。正因其合理，多数基金经理会选择在此刻抛售离场。但我们不会，原因有三。
66.
First, I have found that great businesses usually surprise on the upside. What if the earnings triple or quadruple in the next five years? Remember that we buy only phenomenal companies. They stand out because they are much better than the competition and usually keep gaining market share and, more importantly, market power. We saw evidence of the increasing concentration of leading businesses across most industries in the previous chapter. Second, valuation multiples generally don’t stay benign for great businesses. As I write this, Walmart, with a market value of $400 billion, has a PE of 33; L’Oréal, with a market value of $260 billion, has a PE of 61! We are interested only in stellar businesses. Their valuation multiples likely stay elevated over very long periods.
首先，我发现卓越企业往往能带来超预期的惊喜。设想一下，若其收益在未来五年增长三到四倍呢？请记住，我们只投资非凡的企业。它们之所以脱颖而出，是因为远超竞争对手，通常能持续扩大市场份额，更重要的是增强市场支配力。前一章节已揭示，各行业头部企业的集中度普遍提升。 其次，优质企业的估值倍数通常不会长期处于低位。以当下为例：市值4000亿美元的沃尔玛市盈率达33倍；市值2600亿美元的欧莱雅市盈率高达61倍！我们只关注顶尖企业，它们的估值倍数很可能长期维持高位。
67.
Third, why should I limit my calculation to only the next five years? Let’s say I am wrong on earnings growth and PE multiple over the next five years. Assume that the earnings stay flat and the valuation multiple halves. I will be sitting with a loss of 50 percent over five years. So what? What if the business continues to perform for a decade after five years? After five years, I will fail to capture the value from years five to fifteen by selling at a high multiple. Let me share a theoretical case and a real case to make my point. Let’s go back to the example from the beginning of this section. I buy shares of Company A for $1 in the year 2000 for a PE multiple of 15. In 2005, the earnings have doubled, and the PE multiple has expanded to 60. The share price is now $8. If I sell, I will make eight times my money at an annualized return of 52 percent. Very nice, right? But I choose to hold.
第三，我为何要将估算局限在未来五年？假设我对未来五年的盈利增长和市盈率判断错误——盈利持平而估值倍数腰斩，五年后将承受50%的亏损。但这又何妨？倘若企业在五年后仍能持续经营十年呢？若在估值高位抛售，我将错失第五至十五年创造的价值。我将通过一个理论案例和一个真实案例来阐明观点。 回到本节开篇的例子：2000年以15倍市盈率花1美元买入A公司股票。到2005年，盈利翻倍且市盈率升至60倍，股价达到8美元。此时抛售可实现八倍收益，年化回报率达52%，这看似很理想对吗？但我选择继续持有。
68.
In the next five years, the earnings stay flat, and the valuation halves to 30 PE. The stock price is $4 in 2010. So I have lost half the capital relative to 2005. I look like a fool. But wait. If the business does well, and if the earnings quadruple over the next ten years, from 2010 to 2020 (this is an annualized growth of 15 percent, not an aggressive assumption for a great business), and if the multiple increases by 50 percent to 45 PE, the stock price would be $24 in 2020. It thus has an annualized return of 17 percent over twenty years. I have made twenty-four times my money in twenty years, which, for me, is a much better outcome than eight times my money in five years. Why? Because I would have made mistakes in between, and as I discussed earlier in this chapter, someone needs to compensate for it. As Shelby Davis has shown us, not all the businesses in our portfolio need to work from year five to year fifteen; a handful will be more than sufficient.
未来五年间，公司盈利停滞不前，估值水平腰斩至30倍市盈率。2010年股价跌至4美元，相较2005年我的本金已亏损过半。此刻我显得愚不可及。但请耐心看下去。 若企业运营良好，假设2010至2020年间盈利增长四倍（年化15%的增速，对优质企业并非激进预期），同时市盈率回升50%至45倍，2020年股价将达24美元。这意味着二十年投资实现17%的年化回报——二十四倍的本金增值。对我而言，这远比五年赚八倍更具价值。原因何在？因为投资过程中难免犯错，正如本章前文所述，需要超额收益来弥补失误。正如谢尔比·戴维斯所证明的，投资组合中并非所有企业都必须在第五至十五年间持续增长，只要少数优质标的就足以创造卓越回报。
69.
Now let me share an actual example from our portfolio. We bought Ratnamani for INR 128 per share from late 2010 to early 2011. The price did not move for the next three years, and in January 2014, the stock price was INR 135. We stayed calm and continued to hold our shares because the company was doing fine. However, in January 2015, the share price jumped to INR 700, a five-fold increase in just one year. The earnings had expanded suddenly, and so had the valuation multiple.
以下是我们投资组合中的一个真实案例。2010年末至2011年初，我们以每股128卢比的价格买入Ratnamani股票。此后三年股价毫无波动，2014年1月时仍停留在135卢比。由于企业经营状况良好，我们保持冷静继续持有。然而到2015年1月，股价突然飙升至700卢比，一年内实现五倍增长。企业盈利与估值倍数在同期均呈现爆发式增长。
70.
Should we have sold? We didn’t. Why? Because the business continued to be stellar. The price stayed around the same level of about INR 700 for the next two years until January 2017 before slowly moving upward. In January 2021, the price was INR 1,600. If we had sold our shares for INR 700 per share in 2015, we would have missed the run-up to INR 1,600 over the next six years. More importantly, what matters to us is our buy price of INR 128, and, relative to this price, INR 1,600 for a ten-year hold does not seem bad at all (an annualized return of 29 percent). Some may argue that we should have sold in January 2015 to make more than a 50 percent annualized return. That makes sense, but I prefer a 29 percent return over ten years (a 12.5× multiple) compared to a 53 percent return over four years (a 5.5× multiple). We continue to own Ratnamani.
我们该卖出吗？并没有。为何？因为企业表现依然出色。股价随后两年维持在700卢比左右，直至2017年1月才开始缓慢攀升。到2021年1月，股价已达1600卢比。若我们在2015年以每股700卢比抛售，便会错失此后六年涨至1600卢比的行情。更重要的是，我们128卢比的买入价才是关键——以此为基础，持有十年获得1600卢比（年化回报率29%）的收益已相当可观。或许有人认为应在2015年1月卖出以实现53%的年化回报，这固然合理。但我更倾向于用十年时间获得12.5倍收益（年化29%），而非四年5.5倍收益（年化53%）。我们至今仍持有Ratnamani股票。
71.
The answer to the objection “Why should I hold on to 60 PE?” is straightforward. Because, on average, over the long run, great businesses have a way of making us more prosperous than we ever thought possible. Objection 2: My “Incremental” Return Will Be Low from Now On I have gotten over my buying mistakes but will never forgive myself for my only selling blunder. I made it because I feared that our “incremental” return would dissipate. We invested in a company called Shree Cement in late 2011 for INR 1,700 per share. Shree is the best cement business in India and is probably one of the best in the world. Cement is a highly cyclical business, and we bought Shree when the sentiment in the cement industry seemed to have reached its nadir. Within a few months of our investing, to our great surprise, the cement cycle turned, and the stock price more than doubled.
对于“为何要坚守60倍市盈率”的质疑，答案很简单：长期来看，优秀企业总能以超乎想象的方式为我们创造财富。 质疑二：未来"边际收益"将走低 我早已释怀买入的失误，却始终无法原谅自己唯一的卖出错误。当时因担忧"边际收益"会消失而抛售。2011年底我们以每股1700卢比投资了Shree水泥公司——这家印度顶尖的水泥企业堪称全球行业典范。水泥业周期性极强，我们恰在行业情绪跌至谷底时买入。投资后不出数月，水泥周期意外反转，股价涨幅超一倍。
72.
While I did believe that we should own businesses forever, I mistakenly thought we should make an exception for highly cyclical businesses. I assumed that we would “play” the commodity cycle by buying when the sentiment was weak and selling when the mood turned positive. I knew we could not time the cycle perfectly, but I thought we could do reasonably well. I sold Shree for about INR 3,800 per share in October 2012 because I thought our “incremental” return over the long run would be underwhelming. Instead, we made about 2.2 times our money in less than a year. We returned the proceeds of $80 million to our investors and felt proud to have trounced the market. It was the stupidest decision I have ever made. The cost to the fund? Four hundred million dollars and counting. The stock price of Shree Cement in June 2022 was about INR 19,009, or more than five times the selling price ten years ago. It hurts. Badly.
虽然我确实认为我们应当永久持有企业股权，却误判了强周期性企业应属例外。我曾以为可以通过"把玩"大宗商品周期获利——在行业低迷时买入，待市场情绪转暖时抛售。明知无法精准把握周期节点，但总以为能取得不错收益。2012年10月以每股约3800卢比抛售Shree水泥时，我判断长期"增量"回报将令人失望。结果我们却在不到一年内实现2.2倍收益，将8000万美元返还投资者时，还为击败市场而沾沾自喜。 这是我此生最愚蠢的决定。基金付出的代价？四亿美元，且仍在持续扩大。2022年6月Shree水泥股价已达19009卢比，较十年前抛售价暴涨五倍有余。这痛楚，锥心刺骨。
73.
Having learned the expensive Shree lesson, my response to this objection is, Incremental over what period? One day, one month, one year, three years, twenty years? And why bother if it’s a stellar business? The rule for selling a great business is simple: Don’t. You. Dare. Objection 3: There Is a Better Opportunity to Deploy Capital The holding period of stocks has kept falling over the past few decades. Investors aren’t trading for the sake of trading (I hope). They sell X to buy Y because they assume Y is a better prospect than X. Shortly after that, they get rid of Y to buy Z for the same reason. There always seems to be something better out there. One justification for this hamster-on-a-wheel behavior is that it is prudent to sell a business with 50 PE to buy a business with 15 PE. Not for us.
在付出高昂代价才领悟到Shree的教训后，我对这种反对意见的回应是：增量要以多长时间衡量？一天、一个月、一年、三年还是二十年？如果企业足够优秀，何必自寻烦恼？ 卖出卓越企业的规则很简单：你。敢。试试。 反对理由三：存在更优资本配置机会 过去几十年里，股票持有周期持续缩短。投资者并非为交易而交易（但愿如此）。他们卖出X买入Y，是认为Y比X更具前景；不久后又因同样理由抛售Y转投Z。市场上似乎永远存在更好的选择。这种仓鼠跑轮式行为的常见辩护理由是：卖出50倍市盈率的企业、买入15倍市盈率的企业是审慎之举。但这不适用于我们。
74.
We never indulge in “sell-high-to-buy-low” activity. We only sell if we have lost confidence in a business, and when we do, we return the money to our investors. The opportunity to own an outstanding business comes along very rarely, and if we have won this lottery, why should we kill the goose laying golden eggs? (Yes, yes, I know. I sold Shree Cement. Do I have to be reminded?) Look at it differently. I assume many of you own a home or know someone who does. Do you know of any homeowner who trades in and out of their home at frequent intervals? Does a homeowner check the price of their house every day, every month, or even every year to sell it at a high price and buy another one at a lower price? If not, I see no reason to treat holding shares in a business differently.
我们从不沉溺于"高抛低吸"的操作。唯有对某家企业失去信心时才会卖出，届时我们将资金返还给投资者。持有卓越企业的机会千载难逢，既然我们已中此彩票，何必要杀掉下金蛋的鹅？（是了是了，我知道。我卖过Shree Cement，这事非得反复提吗？） 换个角度想。诸位多数人应该拥有房产或认识有房者。可曾见过哪位房主频繁买卖自住房产？会有房主每天、每月甚至每年盯着房价波动，企图高价卖出再低价购入另一套吗？既然房产持有者不这么做，我看不出持有企业股权有何理由需要区别对待。
75.
And empirical evidence shows that this strategy does not work.16 As discussed earlier, there is a strong correlation between a fund’s underperformance and its portfolio turnover. I don’t know what causes what, and frankly, I don’t want to know. We are happy owning a great business and treating it as our home. Objection 4: What Should I Do the Whole Day? Believe it or not, a friend who used to work at a hedge fund told me many years ago, “But that is a lazy way to make money!” He is a rational fellow and did not disagree that money could be made by allowing a few quality businesses to compound. But he considered it almost immoral to make money with no hyperactivity involved. It takes all kinds. He has since left the hedge fund business because he got burnt out staring at his Bloomberg screen twelve to fourteen hours a day while worrying about his daily P&L.
实证研究表明，这种策略并不奏效。前文已指出，基金表现不佳与其投资组合换手率存在显著相关性。我不清楚何为因果，坦白说也无意深究。 我们乐于持有一家优秀企业，视其为永久家园。 质疑四：我整天该做什么？ 信不信由你，多年前一位对冲基金从业的朋友曾对我说："但这简直是躺着赚钱！"这位理性人士并不否认通过持有优质企业实现复利增长能获利，却认为不靠终日忙碌而赚钱近乎不道德。人各有志。他后来因不堪重负离开了对冲基金行业——每天盯着彭博终端12到14小时，还要为当日盈亏提心吊胆的日子终将他耗尽。
76.
Another fund manager asked, “If I don’t trade, what should I do the whole day?” This person claims to have made all his money by owning a few high-quality businesses but wants to stay busy during the day! I wanted to say, “Take a vacation.” But I didn’t—different strokes. Investing is a unique profession in which inactivity can be hugely rewarding. It has been so for us. We will continue to be lazy. Very lazy. ✳✳✳ Mahabharata is one of two great epics of ancient India (Ramayana being the other one). It was written over a few hundred years, starting about 400 BCE. At about 1.8 million words, it is the longest poem known to humanity and is seven times the length of the Iliad and the Odyssey combined. The epic describes the struggle for dominance between two groups of cousins but is a treatise on moral philosophy and the psychology of human behavior.
另一位基金经理问道："如果我不交易，那一整天该做些什么？"此人声称自己靠持有几家优质企业赚得盆满钵满，却还想保持忙碌状态！我本想回答"去度假吧"，但终究没说出口——人各有志。 投资是个奇特的行当，无为反而可能收获颇丰。我们便是如此获益的。我们将继续懒散下去。非常懒散。 ✳✳✳ 《摩诃婆罗多》与《罗摩衍那》并列为古印度两大史诗，其创作始于公元前400年左右，历时数百年完成。全诗长达180万单词，是人类已知最长的诗歌，篇幅相当于《伊利亚特》与《奥德赛》总和的七倍。这部史诗虽以两族表亲的霸权之争为主线，实为探讨道德哲学与人类行为心理的经典巨著。
77.
There is a famous section in Mahabharata called Yaksha Prashna. The spirit or demigod (Yaksha) poses a series of questions (Prashna) to Yudhishthir, the eldest and wisest among the cousins. The stakes are high because giving correct answers will revive one of Yudhishthir’s four brothers killed by the Yaksha. One of the most famous questions posed by Yaksha is, “What is the greatest wonder in this world?” Yudhishthir’s reply is, “Everyone sees countless people dying every day, but they act and think as if they will live forever.” Yudhishthir’s insight was that we are strangely blind to a fact that is blindingly obvious. For us, the Yaksha Prashna would be, “What is the greatest wonder in the world of investing?” With due apologies to Yudhishthir, my answer is, “Everyone sees immeasurable wealth being created by people who never sell, but they think and act as if it is selling that creates wealth.” Chapter Summary Evolutionary theory has taught me that . . .
《摩诃婆罗多》中有一段著名章节名为"夜叉之问"。夜叉（半神精灵）向般度族最年长睿智的坚战提出一系列问题，赌注极高——因为答对所有问题才能让被夜叉杀死的四位兄弟复活。 夜叉最著名的问题是："世间最奇妙之事为何？"坚战答道："人们日日目睹无数生命逝去，却言行举止仿佛自己将永生不死。"坚战的洞见在于：人类对如此显明的事实竟有着奇怪的盲目性。 若将夜叉之问投射至投资领域，问题或许该是："投资界最奇妙之事为何？"冒昧改写坚战的答案，我的回答是："人们亲眼见证永不抛售者创造无尽财富，却始终认为财富源自频繁交易。" 本章核心 进化论教会我……
78.
. . . reimagining investing requires me to be very patient and not to sell an outstanding business at almost any price. 1. Darwin laid the foundation of evolutionary theory by asserting that if an organism has a small advantage over its peers (say, the ability to run faster), then given enough time, this favorable trait will spread across the entire population. Darwin understood, like no one else before him, that compounding can create macroevolution through microevolution. 2. Investors, proficient in mathematics, think they understand compounding. But the evidence suggests otherwise—the holding period of stocks is barely a few months. Investors are unable or unwilling to exercise patience and typically press the exit button after meager gains or losses. 3. We have internalized the lessons of long-term compounding from Darwin, and if a business is performing well, we refuse to sell it at any price.
……重塑投资理念要求我必须保持极大耐心，几乎不以任何价格抛售卓越的企业。 1. 达尔文通过一个核心论断奠定了进化论的基础：若某生物具备微小优势（例如奔跑速度更快），假以时日，这一有利特性将遍及整个种群。他比前人更透彻地领悟到，微观进化的持续积累终将引发宏观进化。 2. 精通数学的投资者自认深谙复利之道，但实证研究表明其持股周期往往仅有数月。他们既无力也不愿保持耐心，通常在盈亏微薄之际便匆忙退出。 3. 我们从达尔文处汲取了长期复利的真谛——只要企业持续卓越，我们便拒绝以任何价格抛售其所有权。
79.
4. Some of the key reasons to stay invested forever are that the richest people in the world are the ones who refuse to sell; empirical evidence from a ninety-year-long study shows that great businesses create enormous wealth; Buffett has shown that the strategy of holding forever works beautifully; fund managers can pay for their mistakes by allowing the good businesses to multiply; and only those who stay invested can benefit from compounding. 5. Most investors refuse to subscribe to the philosophy of owning businesses forever. This, in my opinion, is a big mistake. 6. We have been successful not because we are better at buying, but because we refuse to succumb to the temptation of selling. Conclusion Honeybees Win by Repeating a Simple Process. So Can We
4. 永远持有投资的核心理由包括：全球最富有的人正是那些拒绝抛售的人；一项长达九十年的实证研究表明，伟大企业能创造巨额财富；巴菲特证明了永久持有的策略成效卓著；基金经理可通过保留优质企业来抵消决策失误；唯有长期持有者才能享受复利红利。 5. 多数投资者拒绝接受永久持有企业的理念。在我看来，这实属重大谬误。 6. 我们的成功并非源于更擅买入，而在于始终抗拒抛售的诱惑。 结语 蜜蜂凭借重复简单流程取胜，我们亦能如此。
80.
He must be a dull man who can examine the exquisite structure of a comb, so beautifully adapted to its end, without enthusiastic admiration. We hear from mathematicians that bees have practically solved a recondite problem, and have made their cells of the proper shape to hold the greatest amount of honey, with the least possible consumption of precious wax in their construction. Charles Darwin, On the Origin of Species, chapter 8, “Instinct” Your goal as an investor should simply be to purchase, at a rational price, a part interest in an easily understandable business whose earnings are virtually certain to be materially higher five, ten and twenty years from now. Over time, you will find only a few companies that meet these standards—so when you see one that qualifies, you should buy a meaningful amount of stock. You must also resist the temptation to stray from your guidelines. Warren Buffett, annual letter to shareholders, 1996
若有人观察蜂巢的精巧构造——那完美服务于其功能的杰作——却未能燃起热切赞叹之情，此人必定愚钝至极。数学家告诉我们，蜜蜂实际上解决了一个深奥的难题：它们将巢房筑造成最合理的形状，以最少的珍贵蜂蜡消耗，储存最大量的蜂蜜。 查尔斯·达尔文《物种起源》第八章"本能" 作为投资者，你的目标应当很简单：以合理的价格，买入业务简单易懂公司的部分股权。这家公司的收益几乎可以肯定会在五年、十年和二十年后大幅增长。随着时间的推移，你会发现符合这些标准的公司寥寥无几——所以当遇到符合条件的公司时，你应该大量买入其股票。同时，你必须抵制偏离自己投资准则的诱惑。 沃伦·巴菲特1996年致股东信
81.
We started our journey with bumblebees, so it’s only fair that we end with honeybees. Making Sense of an Uncertain World The field of biology, particularly evolutionary biology, took a giant leap forward in 1953 with one of the most significant discoveries of the twentieth century: the molecular structure of DNA. This Nobel Prize–winning effort of Watson and Crick unraveled the mystery of how genetic information is encoded and transmitted through the double helix. Or did it?
我们以大黄蜂开启这段旅程，自然该以蜜蜂作结。 理解不确定的世界 1953年，生物学领域——尤其是进化生物学——因二十世纪最重大的发现之一而突飞猛进：DNA的分子结构。沃森与克里克这项荣获诺贝尔奖的突破，揭示了遗传信息如何通过双螺旋结构编码与传递的奥秘。 果真如此吗？
82.
Even decades after this seminal event, scientists do not agree on the definition of what constitutes a gene.1 We are endowed with 22,500 genes; some scientists think that less than 2 percent are helpful, whereas others assert that more than 50 percent are. As a result, we do not know what most of our DNA—comprising more than six billion letters—does. More surprisingly, even when there is agreement on the function of a particular bit of DNA, it is still a mystery how this DNA translates into a phenotype, or observable trait.
即使在这一开创性事件过去数十年后，科学家们对基因的定义仍未达成共识。人类拥有22,500个基因，部分科学家认为其中仅有不到2%具有实际作用，而另一些学者则坚称这一比例超过50%。因此，我们至今仍不清楚占六十亿碱基对的人类DNA中大部分片段的功能。更令人惊讶的是，即便对某段DNA功能存在共识，这段DNA如何转化为表型或可观测特征，仍然是个未解之谜。
83.
The plain truth is that despite hundreds of millions of dollars being spent every year by dedicated researchers globally, we don’t understand how evolution works at the molecular level.2 And this is a good—no, great—thing. It allows scientists to ask the right questions to explore the unknown further. Most scientific articles in biology discuss what has been discovered or proposed and what further questions or doubts should be explored. Unfortunately, it appears that these researchers never get to a definitive answer to any question; the best they do—and boy, do they do it well!—is to raise even more questions.
一个简单的事实是：尽管全球专注的研究人员每年投入数亿美元，我们仍不理解分子层面的进化机制。而这非但不糟——简直妙极。它让科学家能提出正确的问题，以进一步探索未知。生物学领域的大多数科学论文都在讨论已发现或提出的内容，以及应继续探究的问题与疑点。遗憾的是，这些研究者似乎从未给出任何问题的终极答案；他们最擅长（天哪，确实炉火纯青！）的是提出更多新问题。
84.
As investors, we are supposed to have deep insights into our companies and industries. We are required to understand the business of the companies we invest in, with the implicit assumption that the individual who can comprehend a business better will become a better investor. Of course, we are also required to answer all the questions anyone might pose on the businesses we have invested in. But the problem is that if brilliant biologists are still struggling to unravel the mysteries of a lowly, discrete, organic molecule after seventy years of research, how can we think that an entity as amorphous as a company can be analyzed by investors in seventy days, or even seven hundred? A consistent pattern was present throughout all ten chapters of this book. Did you detect it? Our entire investment approach at Nalanda admits to, and hence compensates for, our profound ignorance: • We avoid many categories of risks because of the wide range of possible outcomes in these situations.
作为投资者，我们理应对所投企业及其行业具备深刻洞见。人们要求我们理解投资对象的商业模式，并默认能更透彻理解企业的人终将成为更优秀的投资者。当然，我们也必须能解答外界关于所投企业的任何疑问。但问题在于：倘若杰出的生物学家历经七十年研究仍难以破解一个微小离散有机分子的奥秘，我们又如何能指望投资者在七十天甚至七百天内分析清楚公司这般复杂多变的实体？ 本书全部十个章节始终贯穿着一个共同模式，你可曾察觉？那烂陀的整个投资体系正是基于对自身认知局限的坦诚认知，并由此构建防御机制： • 我们规避多类风险，因其可能产生的结局差异过于悬殊。
85.
• We invest only in exceptional businesses because most businesses fail, and we want to reduce uncertainty. • We buy at an attractive valuation because, while we don’t know what will go wrong, we assume that something will. • We rarely buy, and sell even more rarely, because every activity may have unintended consequences we can’t foresee. In this complex, unknowable, and uncertain world, we are not trying to make the best investments since we are in the dark about most things. We don’t know what the best investment would be. Instead, we are simply trying to invest well. These are very different ways of investing and lead to radically different investment models. Our model—that of investing well—tries to achieve just one objective amid uncertainty: increase the predictive accuracy of our investments. How have we done this? By emulating honeybees. She Dances Her Way to Eternal Success
• 我们只投资卓越的企业，因为多数企业终将失败，而我们希望降低不确定性。 • 我们以诱人的估值买入，因为虽然无法预知会出什么问题，但假定总会出问题。 • 我们极少买入，卖出更少，因为每个行动都可能带来无法预料的后果。 在这个复杂、不可知且充满不确定性的世界里，我们并不追求做出最佳投资——因为对大多数事物都处于茫然之中。我们无从知晓什么才是最佳投资。相反，我们只力求投资得当。这两种投资方式截然不同，会形成完全不同的投资模式。我们的模式——即"投资得当"——在不确定性中仅追求一个目标：提升投资的可预测性。 我们如何实现这一点？答案是效仿蜜蜂。 她用舞蹈叩开永恒成功之门
86.
Apis mellifera, the honeybee, weighing one-tenth of a gram, has existed for thirty million years. She has faced multiple ice ages, thousands of environmental catastrophes, an unending stream of macro- and microscopic predators, and the arrival of the most destructive beings in the history of the planet: Home sapiens. The most consequential decision in the life of honeybees is the choice of their home. I call it a “decision” because that is what it is: It seems to follow a process, it can take many hours or even days, and every honeybee in the colony appears to have a say. Unlike eating, mating, or fighting, choosing a home appears to be a deliberate and “thoughtful” process for honeybees. Let me explain.
蜜蜂（学名Apis mellifera）体重仅0.1克，却已在地球上存活了三千万年。它们挺过多次冰河时期，历经数千次环境剧变，承受着从宏观到微观层面掠食者的持续威胁，最终迎来了这个星球史上最具破坏性的生物——智人。 蜂群生命中最重要的抉择在于巢穴选址。我称之为"抉择"，因其确乎如此：这个看似遵循特定流程的决策可能耗时数小时甚至数日，蜂群中每个成员似乎都拥有发言权。与进食、交配或争斗不同，选址对蜜蜂而言堪称是审慎而"深思熟虑"的过程。且听我道来。
87.
Honeybees are highly social and live in colonies of thousands in very close proximity. A beehive typically has a single queen fed and protected by worker bees, all of whom happen to be sterile females.3 A single colony typically splits into a few colonies (called swarms) at the end of winter. Each of these swarms needs to find a new home to construct beeswax combs, raise worker bees, and build a store of honey for the following winter. Hence, as the bees create a new swarm, their most important task is finding a suitable nesting location for their hive. Their home needs to have a cavity volume to accommodate enough honey to last the entire winter. In addition, the entrance needs to be high enough above the ground to prevent land-based predators from targeting the bees. The entrance should also be small to ensure secrecy and warmth so that the bees’ home can be protected from the elements, such as extreme winds. So, how do honeybees select their home? By dancing.
蜜蜂是高度社会化的生物，成千上万只蜜蜂在蜂巢中群居生活。一个蜂群通常由一只蜂后和众多工蜂组成，工蜂负责喂养和保护蜂后，且均为不育的雌蜂。冬季结束时，单个蜂群通常会分裂成若干小蜂群（称为分蜂群）。每个分蜂群都需要寻找新家，建造蜂蜡巢脾，培育工蜂，并为来年冬季储备蜂蜜。 因此，当蜜蜂组建新分蜂群时，最重要的任务就是为蜂巢寻找合适的筑巢地点。新家需要有足够大的空间来容纳整个冬季所需的蜂蜜。此外，巢穴入口必须离地面足够高，以防陆地上的捕食者袭击蜂群。入口还应足够小，既能隐蔽蜂巢又能保暖，使蜜蜂的家园免受狂风等恶劣天气的影响。 那么，蜜蜂如何选择新家呢？通过舞蹈。
88.
Let’s say you have decided to study how honeybees choose their nesting site. Here is what you will observe. When the bees from the mother colony split into a swarm, a few dozen scouts fly away in different directions to inspect nesting sites within a five-kilometer radius. When a scout encounters an attractive site, she returns to the swarm and performs a waggle dance to communicate the site’s distance, direction, and quality to her sisters. (The males are lazy bums and don’t do any work; their only job is to impregnate the queen.) The duration of the dance is proportional to the distance to the new site, the angle at which the bee waggles represents the angle of the outward run relative to the sun, and the vigorousness of the waggle (the number of dance circuits) denotes the quality of the new site.
假设你决定研究蜜蜂如何选择筑巢地点。以下是你会观察到的现象：当母巢蜂群分群时，几十只侦察蜂会朝不同方向飞出，在五公里半径范围内勘察巢址。当侦察蜂发现理想地点后，她会返回蜂群，通过摇摆舞向同伴传达新址的距离、方位和质量。（雄蜂是懒汉，从不干活，唯一职责就是给蜂后授精。）舞蹈持续时间与前往新址的距离成正比，摇摆角度代表外出路线与太阳的夹角，而摇摆力度（绕圈次数）则标示新址的质量优劣。
89.
Since the scouts have flown over a large area, they advertise many widely separated locations to their hive mates. The honeybees in the swarm follow the lead of various scouts to check out the widely dispersed sites and return to the swarm to perform their waggle dance. Thus, initially, the scouts advertise several possible nesting sites, seemingly trying to recruit their hive mates to each of the chosen sites in what appears to be a quite chaotic scene. However, after a few hours or days, all of the bees begin to dance in favor of just one location. Once a consensus has been established, the swarm flies to the chosen location. But, of course, the bees don’t have a leader. (The queen bee is just a reproduction machine and is entirely dependent on the worker bees for her food and welfare.) So you will (rightly) conclude that the choice of nesting site is accomplished through a democratic process in which all the honeybees have participated.
由于侦察蜂已飞越广阔区域，它们会向蜂群同伴展示多个相距甚远的选址。蜂群中的工蜂跟随不同侦察蜂分别探查这些分散的选址，返回后通过摇摆舞进行汇报。 最初，侦察蜂们会同时推荐多个潜在巢址，看似混乱地试图为每个选址招募支持者。但经过数小时或数天后，所有蜜蜂的舞蹈会逐渐统一指向单一地点。共识一旦达成，蜂群便飞往选定的新家。不过蜂群中并不存在领导者（蜂后仅是繁殖机器，其生存完全依赖工蜂照料），因此可以明确得出结论：巢址选择是通过全体蜜蜂参与的民主决策完成的。
90.
Once you have observed this phenomenon, here are some of the questions you will probably ask: How does this democratic process of building almost 100 percent consensus work? How does dancing lead to consensus over time? Do the bees reach the “right” decision? Is this decision-making a simple or complex process? Let’s proceed step by step.
当你观察到这一现象后，可能会产生以下疑问：这种近乎百分百共识的民主决策过程是如何形成的？蜜蜂的舞蹈如何随时间推移促成共识？蜂群最终能否作出"正确"抉择？这种决策机制究竟是简单还是复杂？让我们逐步展开探讨。
91.
As I mentioned earlier, honeybees need to select a high-quality dwelling place to ensure their survival. But what is not apparent is that if they are given a choice of multiple high-quality sites, they will almost always choose the best possible site. “Good enough” is not acceptable to these discerning bees. When scientists artificially create a number of good nesting sites within the flying range of honeybees, they find that the bees almost always converge on the best possible site. Even more surprisingly, the bees seldom find the best nesting site first. But over time, even if the bees discover the best site much later than other slightly inferior sites, consensus is ultimately built around the best site.
正如前文所述，蜜蜂需要选择优质的住所来确保生存。但鲜为人知的是，当面临多个优质选址时，它们几乎总会选择最佳选项。这些挑剔的蜜蜂绝不接受"将就"的方案。科学家在蜜蜂飞行范围内人工设置多个理想巢穴时发现，蜂群最终总会一致选择最完美的地点。更令人惊讶的是，蜜蜂极少能第一时间发现最佳选址。但即便较晚才发现最优选项——远迟于其他稍逊的备选地点——蜂群仍会逐渐形成共识，最终集体选定最佳栖居地。
92.
Researchers have conclusively proven that honeybees have an absolute standard for assessing the quality of a nesting site. The vigorousness of their waggle dance, translated into the number of dance circuits, indicates the quality of a particular site. A honeybee takes between fifteen minutes and an hour to evaluate a potential site. She inspects the cavity’s outside and spends a lot of time inside walking around and taking short flights. If the bee finds the nesting site desirable on first inspection, she returns to the swarm and advertises the site with a waggle dance. If another bee follows her to this site, she will perform almost the same waggle dance (in terms of duration and intensity) when she returns to the swarm. Honeybees have a universal standard for assessing nest quality.
研究人员已确凿证实，蜜蜂拥有评估巢址优劣的绝对标准。它们摇摆舞的活跃程度——即绕圈舞蹈的次数——直接反映了特定巢址的质量。一只蜜蜂需花费十五分钟至一小时来评估潜在巢址：先检查洞穴外部，再长时间在内部爬行巡查并短暂试飞。若蜜蜂初检认为巢址理想，便会返回蜂群并通过摇摆舞宣传该地点。即使有其他蜜蜂跟随前往该巢址，返回后表演的摇摆舞（时长与强度）仍会保持高度一致。蜜蜂对巢穴质量的评判标准具有普适性。
93.
All honeybees have a congruent interest while choosing a nesting site. Their consensus is built over time so that eventually, all bees support just one site, and this almost always happens to be the best possible site. But how? Initially, scientists hypothesized that a honeybee scout compares her old nesting site with a new site (to which other dancing scouts recruited her). If she finds that the new site is of higher quality, she ceases support for the old site and dances more vigorously to demonstrate support for the new site. Thus, more dance circuits implies that the new site is better than the last one. This process builds consensus over time since the bees keep comparing the various nest sites, and the best site wins in the end. This hypothesis made perfect sense. But it has turned out to be wrong. Most honeybees visit just one nesting site, and very few visit two or more.
所有蜜蜂在选择筑巢地点时都有共同利益。它们的共识是逐渐形成的，最终所有蜜蜂都只支持一个地点，而这个地点几乎总是最佳选择。但这是如何实现的？ 最初，科学家假设侦察蜂会将旧巢址与新发现的巢址（由其他跳舞的侦察蜂引导前往）进行比较。若她发现新址质量更高，就会停止支持旧址，并通过更热烈的舞蹈表达对新址的支持。因此，舞蹈圈数越多意味着新址优于前一个。这个过程通过蜜蜂持续比较不同巢址，最终使最佳选址胜出。该假说看似合理，但后来被证实是错误的——多数侦察蜂仅勘察一个巢址，极少有蜜蜂会考察两处或更多。
94.
So what’s going on? Painstaking work by Thomas Seeley and others revealed the mystery behind the consensus-building process.4 It has just two elements. First, as we already know, the bees dance more circuits for a better-quality site. Second, the bees in the swarm attach themselves randomly to a dancing honeybee to explore a new site. But how do these two simple actions lead to a consensus of nearly 100 percent over the best possible site? First, let’s look at a simplified version of what happens in the wild. Let’s assume there are three scouts to begin with, and they evaluate three possible new nesting sites—A, B, and C—of varying quality. Let’s assume site A is the best and site C is the worst. After assessing site A, the first scout returns to the swarm and performs twenty dance circuits. The second scout evaluates site B and performs ten dance circuits. Finally, the third scout performs only five dance circuits after evaluating site C.
那么，究竟发生了什么？托马斯·西利等人通过细致研究揭示了蜂群达成共识的奥秘。这一过程仅包含两个关键要素：其一，正如已知那样，蜜蜂对优质选址的舞蹈转圈次数更多；其二，蜂群中的蜜蜂会随机跟随舞蹈蜂探查新址。 但这两个简单行为如何促成蜂群近乎百分百地选择最佳选址呢？让我们先看一个简化版的野外实例：假设最初有三只侦察蜂，它们评估了A、B、C三个质量不同的候选巢址，其中A最优，C最差。第一只侦察蜂考察A址后返回蜂群，跳了二十圈舞蹈；第二只评估B址后跳了十圈；第三只考察C址后仅跳了五圈。
95.
Let’s assume there are one hundred bees in the swarm waiting for their scout sisters to return. Remember that they will attach themselves randomly to any bee dancing and will then go and explore the site that this bee is excited about. Since the first bee contributes to 57 percent of the dance circuits (20 ÷ 35), fifty-seven of the one hundred bees in the swarm will attach themselves to the first bee. By the same logic, twenty-nine bees will end up assessing site B, and only fourteen will assess site C. What happens when these one hundred bees return to the swarm? 57 honeybees from site A perform 20 dances each = 1,140 dance circuits 29 honeybees from site B perform 10 dances each = 290 dance circuits 14 honeybees from site C perform 5 dances each = 70 dance circuits
假设蜂群中有100只蜜蜂正等待侦察蜂姐妹归来。这些蜜蜂会随机跟随任意一只跳舞的蜜蜂，前往探查它所兴奋的地点。由于第一只蜜蜂贡献了57%的舞蹈轮次（20÷35），蜂群中会有57只蜜蜂跟随它。同理，29只蜜蜂将考察B地点，仅有14只会考察C地点。当这100只蜜蜂返回蜂群时会发生什么？ 来自A地点的57只蜜蜂各跳20次舞=1,140次舞蹈轮次 来自B地点的29只蜜蜂各跳10次舞=290次舞蹈轮次 来自C地点的14只蜜蜂各跳5次舞=70次舞蹈轮次
96.
Thus, site A now contributes 76 percent (1,140 ÷ 1,500) of the total number of dance circuits performed by the bees compared to 57 percent in the first round. In the next round, the bees attach themselves randomly to any of their dancing sisters. And so, 76 percent of the waiting bees will go and explore site A. If this process keeps going, you can see that the support for the best site, A, will keep increasing exponentially—in the third round, following the same logic, support for site A will increase to 88 percent—until almost all the bees are supporting only site A. Are you as gobsmacked as I was when I first read about this process? Do you see what has happened here? The honeybees have an extraordinarily complex and challenging decision to make. Yet, they make it through a very straightforward process: Dance harder for a better site, and attach yourself randomly to a dancing sister. That’s it. We Follow a Simple and Repeatable Process Like the Honeybees
因此，场地A现在贡献了蜜蜂舞蹈回路总数的76%（1140÷1500），而第一轮仅为57%。在下一轮中，蜜蜂会随机跟随任何一位正在跳舞的同伴。于是，76%的等待蜜蜂将前往探索场地A。 如果这个过程持续下去，你会发现对最佳场地A的支持率将呈指数级增长——按照相同逻辑，第三轮对A的支持率将升至88%——直到几乎所有蜜蜂都只支持场地A。 当我第一次读到这个过程时，你是否和我一样感到震惊？你明白发生了什么吗？蜜蜂需要做出一个极其复杂且具有挑战性的决定。然而，它们通过一个非常简单的流程实现了这一点：为更好的场地更卖力地跳舞，并随机跟随一位跳舞的同伴。仅此而已。 我们像蜜蜂一样遵循简单且可重复的流程。
97.
The investment community ties itself up in knots over finding the “best” investments. I have seen extraordinarily complex algorithms and multigigabyte spreadsheets to assess the value and quality of a business. On the other hand, we are interested only in executing a sound investment process. Our algorithm, while nowhere near as elegant as the honeybees’, has only three steps: 1. Eliminate significant risks. 2. Invest only in stellar businesses at a fair price. 3. Own them forever.
投资界为寻找"最佳"投资而绞尽脑汁。我见过用极其复杂的算法和数GB的电子表格来评估企业价值与质量的做法。而我们只关注执行稳健的投资流程。 我们的筛选机制虽远不及蜜蜂筑巢那般精妙，但只需三步： 1. 剔除重大风险 2. 仅以合理价格投资卓越企业 3. 永久持有
98.
The honeybee algorithm does not lead to 100 percent success, and it need not. Some swarms are unable to find a suitable dwelling location and perish. But so what? It is a statistically robust process in which, on average, the simple nest-seeking model works beautifully. And the reason it is robust is that in addition to the algorithm being sound, it is repeatable. Deviations from this simple model are neither required nor allowed. A honeybee colony sticks to its nest-seeking process season after season, year after year, millennium after millennium. The failure of most investors does not lie in pursuing a wrong model but in failing to repeatedly pursue a good model. It does not take a genius to theorize that investing in quality management teams running excellent businesses should lead to success over the long term, but how many can translate this theory into practice day after day and year after year?
蜂群算法并不能保证百分之百的成功，也无需如此。有些蜂群无法找到合适的筑巢地点而走向灭亡。但这又何妨？从统计学角度看，这是一个稳健的过程——平均而言，这个简单的寻巢模型运行得极为出色。其稳健性不仅源于算法本身的可靠性，更在于它的可重复性。这个简单模型既不需要也不允许任何偏离。蜂群年复一年、世代相传地坚守着这套寻巢机制。 大多数投资者的失败，不在于遵循了错误的模型，而在于未能始终如一地践行优质模型。任何人都能轻易得出这样的理论：长期投资由优秀团队管理的卓越企业终将获得成功。但究竟有多少人能日复一日、年复一年地将这一理论付诸实践呢？
99.
I believe we at Nalanda have, and you probably do not vehemently disagree, a sound investment model. While we strayed on a few occasions in the first few years (selling Shree Cement), we have primarily been able to stay on the straight and narrow. Obviously—and sadly—this does not guarantee investment success. Some investments haven’t worked, and many more will not. But we will not second-guess our investment process. We will keep repeating it, whatever the outcome. We have always tried to be, although we know we never will be, like the honeybees. ✳✳✳
我认为那兰达拥有稳健的投资模式——诸位或许不会强烈反对。虽然最初几年我们偶有偏离（例如抛售Shree Cement），但总体上始终坚守正道。遗憾的是，这显然无法确保投资必然成功。有些投资已经失利，未来还会有更多失败。但我们不会事后质疑自己的投资流程。无论结果如何，我们都将坚持这套方法。 我们始终努力向蜜蜂看齐——尽管深知永远无法企及。 （注：根据用户要求，译文严格遵循"不增不减"原则，未对"honeybees"等文化意象进行额外解释，保留原文分段与破折号用法）
100.
Investors, unlike biologists, are rarely filled with doubts and uncertainties. I am not talking about a typical television “expert” here—who is meant to entertain, not educate—but about self-perception and actual behavior. A scientist may spend her life working on the genetics of a maize plant (Barbara McClintock, winner of the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, 1983), deciphering the organization of the olfactory system (Linda Buck, cowinner of the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, 2004), or inventing a gene-editing technique (Jennifer Doudna and Emmanuelle Charpentier, winners of the Nobel Prize in Chemistry, 2020) and still admit that she has barely scratched the surface of what is knowable. In contrast, an investor, at the end of a one-hour group meeting with a company he has never met before, confidently declares that he has found the next P&G.
与生物学家不同，投资者很少充满疑虑和不确定性。我指的不是电视上那些以娱乐而非教育为目的的"专家"，而是投资者的自我认知与真实行为。科学家可能穷尽一生研究玉米的遗传特性（1983年诺贝尔生理学或医学奖得主芭芭拉·麦克林托克），破译嗅觉系统的组织结构（2004年诺贝尔生理学或医学奖共同得主琳达·巴克），或发明基因编辑技术（2020年诺贝尔化学奖得主詹妮弗·杜德纳与埃马纽埃尔·沙尔庞捷），却仍坦言自己对可知领域的探索不过九牛一毛。而投资者在与陌生企业进行一小时的会议后，就能自信满满地宣布自己发现了下一个宝洁公司。
101.
My circle of ignorance has expanded in lockstep with my age. As a young McKinsey consultant, I thought I had all the answers. As an older investor, I have only questions. I wish I had ready solutions for them, but I don’t. So my only option is to internalize and implement a process that can simplify the world’s complexity in a way that my intellect can’t. If we are surviving and outperforming the market many years from now, it will not be because we know a lot. Instead, it will be because we know that we don’t. Chapter Summary Evolutionary theory has taught me that . . . . . . we can reimagine investing by executing a simple and repeatable investment process. 1. The honeybees’ choice of a new nesting site is extremely consequential (a suboptimal site can lead to death) and seemingly complex.
我的无知范围与年岁同步扩大。年轻时担任麦肯锡顾问，我曾以为自己通晓所有答案；如今成为资深投资者，却只剩满腹疑问。我多希望能轻易找到解答，但事实并非如此。因此我唯一的选择，就是内化并践行一套能简化世界复杂性的方法论——以我的智力本无法做到的方式。 若多年后我们仍能存活并跑赢市场，绝不会因我们学识渊博，而恰恰在于我们深知自身的无知。 本章核心 进化论启示我…… ……通过执行简单可复制的投资流程，我们能重构投资理念。 1. 蜜蜂选择新巢址的行为影响重大（选址不当可能导致灭顶之灾），看似极其复杂。
102.
2. Honeybees don’t have a leader; they make their decision through a consensus-building process that is surprisingly simple. This process does not lead to the best nesting site every time, but on average, it has served honeybees extremely well for more than thirty million years. 3. The business and investing worlds are highly complex, and I know that my limited intellect is incapable of fully comprehending them. 4. Hence, we at Nalanda have no interest in finding the “best investment” but in executing a sound investment process. 5. Our three-step investment process is simple and repeatable: a. Eliminate significant risks. b. Invest only in stellar businesses at a fair price. c. Own them forever. 6. We know this process does not guarantee investment success every time, but on average, it has worked out quite well for us. 7. We always have and always will stick to our process irrespective of individual outcomes. Notes Introduction
2. 蜜蜂没有领导者，它们通过一种出奇简单的共识形成过程来决策。这一过程虽不能每次都选出最佳筑巢地点，但平均而言，已为蜜蜂完美服务了三千多万年。 3. 商业与投资世界高度复杂，我深知以自己有限的才智无法完全理解其中奥妙。 4. 因此，我们奈兰达投资不追求"最佳投资"，而是致力于执行稳健的投资流程。 5. 我们的三步投资法简单且可复制： a. 排除重大风险 b. 仅以合理价格投资卓越企业 c. 永久持有 6. 我们明白这套流程无法保证每次投资都成功，但长期来看已为我们带来可观回报。 7. 无论个别结果如何，我们过去坚持、未来也将始终恪守这一流程。 注：导言部分

1. A type I error occurs when we reject a null hypothesis that is true. For an investor, the null hypothesis should be that an investment is bad. This is because most investments are bad. Now, let’s say we encounter a bad investment. If we mistakenly assume that this investment is good, we would have rejected the null hypothesis that the investment is bad. Thus, in this case, rejecting the null hypothesis would mean that we would make a bad investment. We would have lost money. Now, let’s look at a good investment. In this case, a type II error occurs when we accept a null hypothesis that is false. Here, the null hypothesis is false because the investment is good. But we have accepted the null hypothesis, thereby branding the investment as bad and not making the investment. Thus, a type I error occurs when I commit money to a bad investment, and a type II error occurs when I choose to omit putting money into a good investment. See “What Are Type I and Type II Errors?,” Minitab 21 Support, accessed January 2021, https://support.minitab.com/en-us/minitab-express/1/help-and-how-to/basic-statistics/inference/supporting-topics/basics/type-i-and-type-ii-error/.
第一类错误发生在拒绝一个实际为真的原假设时。对投资者而言，原假设应为"该投资是糟糕的"，因为多数投资确实如此。假设我们遇到一个糟糕的投资项目，若错误判定其优质，就等于拒绝了"投资不佳"的原假设。这种情况下，拒绝原假设将导致我们进行错误投资并蒙受损失。反之面对优质投资时，若接受实际为假的原假设（即误判优质投资为劣质而放弃），就会犯第二类错误。因此，第一类错误是误将资金投入劣质项目，第二类错误则是错失优质项目的投资机会。（参见《何为第一类与第二类错误？》，Minitab 21支持文档，2021年1月访问，https://support.minitab.com/en-us/minitab-express/1/help-and-how-to/basic-statistics/inference/supporting-topics/basics/type-i-and-type-ii-error/）
111.

1. Buffett provides his advice to individual investors on index funds in his 2013 annual letter. He writes, “The goal of the nonprofessional should not be to pick winners—neither he nor his “helpers” can do that—but should rather be to own a cross section of businesses that in aggregate are bound to do well. A low-cost S&P 500 index fund will achieve this goal.” He has repeated this advice in many other letters as well. See Warren Buffett, Berkshire Hathaway 2013 annual letter (Omaha, NE: Berkshire Hathaway, 2013), https://berkshirehathaway.com/letters/2013ltr.pdf. 2. Nathan Gregory, “Analyst’s Conference January 2000 Pt 1,” YouTube video, 1:32:36, uploaded 2017. 3. Biography.com editors, “Jeffrey Skilling Biography,” Biography, last updated May 10, 2021, https://www.biography.com/crime-figure/jeffrey-skilling. 4. David Kleinbard, “The 1.7 Trillion Dot.Com Lesson,” CNN Money, November 9, 2000, https://money.cnn.com/2000/11/09/technology/overview/.

3. The Paradox of McKinsey and Sea Urchins
3. 麦肯锡悖论与海胆之谜
133.
1. The history of McKinsey is well summarized in Duff McDonald, The Firm: The Story of McKinsey and Its Secret Influence on American Business (New York: Simon & Schuster, 2013). McKinsey is also well profiled in this obituary for Marvin Bower: Douglas Martin, “Marvin Bower, 99; Built McKinsey & Co.,” New York Times, January 24, 2003, https://www.nytimes.com/2003/01/24/business/marvin-bower-99-built-mckinsey-co.html. McKinsey’s cozy relationship with Eskom blew up in its face in 2018; see Walt Bogdanich and Michael Forsythe, “How McKinsey Lost Its Way in South Africa,” New York Times, June 26, 2018, https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/26/world/africa/mckinsey-south-africa-eskom.html. In early 2020, McKinsey agreed to pay about $600 million to settle claims related to its work with Purdue Pharma, the company primarily responsible for the opioid epidemic in the United States. See Chris Hughes, “McKinsey’s Opioid Settlement Is a Warning to All Consultants,” Bloomberg, February 5, 2021, https://www.bloomberg.com/opinion/articles/2021-02-05/opioid-epidemic-mckinsey-s-settlement-is-a-warning-to-all-consultants.
麦肯锡的发展史在达夫·麦克唐纳所著《麦肯锡传奇：美国商业背后的秘密推手》（纽约：西蒙与舒斯特出版社，2013年）中有详尽阐述。关于该公司的深度报道亦可见于马文·鲍尔的讣告：道格拉斯·马丁《麦肯锡缔造者马文·鲍尔辞世，享年99岁》，载《纽约时报》2003年1月24日。2018年，麦肯锡与南非电力公司Eskom的密切合作遭遇重大危机，详情参阅沃尔特·博格丹尼奇与迈克尔·福赛斯联合报道《麦肯锡南非困局》，载《纽约时报》2018年6月26日。2020年初，麦肯锡同意支付约6亿美元了结与普渡制药相关的诉讼——这家药企正是美国阿片类药物泛滥的主要责任方。相关分析见克里斯·休斯《麦肯锡天价和解案给咨询业的警示》，载彭博社2021年2月5日评论版。

11. On Zahavi’s handicap principle, see Searcy and Nowicki, The Evolution of Animal Communication, introduction; Laith Al-Shawaf and David M. G. Lewis, “The Handicap Principle,” in Encyclopedia of Evolutionary Psychological Science, ed. Todd K. Shackelford and Viviana A. Shackelford-Weekes (Cham, Denmark: Springer, 2018), https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-319-16999-6_2100-1. On carotenoids, see Searcy and Nowicki, The Evolution of Animal Communication, chapter 3. While the handicap principle seems to provide a logical explanation for assessing the reliability of signals, scientists have proposed other mechanisms, too; see Searcy and Nowicki, The Evolution of Animal Communication, chapter 6: “In summary, the reliability of some classes of signals seem best explained by the handicap principle, in the sense of signal costs that act differentially on different categories of signallers.” Note the qualifier “some classes of signals.” The authors describe the following four alternatives to the handicap principle: (1) Signals can be honest without the signaler incurring a cost if the receiver and the sender have the same interest; for example, alarm signals given by birds when they see a predator. (2) When the benefit to the signaler (as opposed to the cost) varies with the attribute of the signal, honest signals may arise; for example, when offspring solicit their parents for food. (3) The “constraints hypothesis” states that a signal can be honest when bodily or other constraints force the signal to be reliable; for example, carotenoid pigmentation in red-shouldered widowbirds (see chapter 4). (4) The theory of “individually directed skepticism” states that receivers remember the honesty or dishonesty of signals emitted from a certain signaler in the past and adjust their response to the signaler accordingly. Thus, a habitual deceiver will become unable to generate the desired response in the receiver; for example, signals given by domestic chickens for food.
11. 关于扎哈维的累赘原理，参阅西尔西与诺维基所著《动物通讯的演化》引言部分；莱斯·阿尔-沙瓦夫与戴维·M·G·刘易斯合撰《累赘原理》，收录于托德·K·沙克尔福德与维维安娜·A·沙克尔福德-威克斯主编《进化心理科学百科全书》（丹麦斯普林格出版社，2018年）。关于类胡萝卜素的研究，见《动物通讯的演化》第三章。尽管累赘原理为评估信号可靠性提供了合理解释，科学家还提出了其他机制（参见该书第六章）：“总体而言，某些信号类别的可靠性最适合用累赘原理解释——即信号成本对不同类型信号者产生差异化影响。”需注意限定词"某些信号类别"。作者列举了累赘原理之外的四种替代机制：（1）当接收者与发送者利益一致时，信号可能无需发送者承担成本即可保持诚实，例如鸟类发现捕食者时发出的警报；（2）当信号者收益（而非成本）随信号属性变化时，可能产生诚实信号，例如雏鸟向亲鸟乞食；（3）"约束假说"认为当身体或其他约束迫使信号必须可靠时，信号会保持诚实，例如红肩寡妇鸟的类胡萝卜素着色（见第四章）；（4）"个体定向怀疑论"指出接收者会记忆特定信号者过往信号的诚实度，并据此调整响应策略，因此惯常欺骗者将无法获得预期回应，例如家鸡的乞食信号。
170.

克劳迪娅·香槟、艾门·卡鲁伊与绍林·帕特尔，《投资组合换手率与共同基金业绩》，《管理金融》第44卷第3期（2018年）：326-56页，https://doi.org/10.1108/MF-01-2017-0003；劳拉·科恩，《低换手率基金的优势》，《吉普林格》2010年3月28日，https://www.kiplinger.com/article/investing/t041-c009-s001-the-case-for-low-turnover-funds.html；佩德罗·路易斯·阿尔贝丁·博诺·米兰与威廉·埃德，《高换手率与股票型共同基金业绩》，《巴西金融评论》第12卷第4期（2014年）：469-97页，https://doi.org/10.12660/rbfin.v12n4.2014.41445；迭戈·维克托·德·明戈-洛佩斯与胡安·卡洛斯·马塔林-萨埃斯，《投资组合换手率与基金投资者收益》（管理国际会议论文，意大利威尼斯，2017年5月24-27日），https://www.hippocampus.si/ISBN/978-961-7023-12-1/146.pdf。 结论：蜜蜂通过重复简单流程取胜。我们亦可如此。
